title (
Bestiary of Hyrule
)
head (
# Bestiary of Hyrule ((Bestiary of Hyrule))
-
)
pagenumbers

The world of the Legend of Zelda is home to many fascinating and unique creatures, many of which are monsters that stand in the way of heroes.  Using these creatures in a Pathfinder 2e campaign that is not a Legend of Zelda campaign may cause some dissonance, but with some flavor tweaks they could be used in a non-Zelda campaign without issue.  The same is true for using base Pathfinder 2e monsters in a Legend of Zelda campaign.

If a creature in this bestiary appears in multiple games with different traits, then the resulting creature will be an amalgamation of all the official depictions, or multiple variants of the creature will be listed.

### Differently Leveled Creatures
If you want to use a creature found in this bestiary, but of a different level, you can use the **Building Creatures** rules, found starting on page 56 in the *Gamemastery Guide* to adjust the statistics to match the new level.

All creature levels are set by a somewhat arbitrary metric based on approximately when a monster is encountered in a Zelda game, with some exceptions.  However, as the Legend of Zelda series is not an RPG (it's an action-adventure series), there are no official levels attached to monsters that could be used to approximate a proper level scaling.

### Companion to Adventures in Hyrule
This document is designed to be used as a standalone document, but it is also intended to be used as the bestiary to Aoife Ester's [Adventures in Hyrule](http://scribe.pf2.tools/v/wXO8Df9X) homebrew document for Legend of Zelda campaigns.

### Non-Canon Abilities
While most statblocks will try to adhere as much to game canon as possible, due to the nature of a tabletop game versus a video game, some liberty will be taken with statblocks.  New abilities may be added that make sense for a creature based on its physiology or to make it more capable to fight against a party of Heroes rather than a single Hero.

|
note (
# Key Terms.
You'll see the following key terms and traits throughout this document.
    **Vulnerability:** The vulnerability trait is used to indicate a specific vulnerability of a creature that may be triggered by targeting a specific location on the creature or by using a specific item or weapon.
)

### Vulnerable Spots
Some creatures have a vulnerable spot, such as an eye, that can be targeted for extra effects.  This is to simulate the Legend of Zelda boss weak point system.  Vulnerable spots will have the ***vulnerability*** trait on them.  Typically these will be called out in the statblock and require a -2 circumstance penalty to aim for the weak spot in return for extra damage or bypassing resistances and/or immunities.

A player can use the Recall Knowledge action to try and identify a Vulnerable Spot on a creature that has one. The GM can provide the player with the Vulnerable Spot in lieu of other best known attributes of the creature.

### Alignment Post-Remaster?
Alignment was left in for each creature despite alignment being removed in the Remaster for Pathfinder 2e for legacy reasons.  There are GMs and players who prefer to play with the old alignment system and so alignment on creatures is preserved for people who want to use that system.  If you want to be fully Remaster compatible, simply ignore the alignment trait in all statblocks.
=
# Ache ((+Ache))

## Ache ((++Ache))
Called "Eyes of Ganon" by townsfolk, Aches can disguise themselves in the villages of Hyrule as ordinary Hylians. Almost anyone you talk to may be an Ache in disguise, and they often reveal themselves and attack when talked to, striking unexpectedly.
right(
# Eyes of Ganon
Aches act as spies and messengers for the dark lord Ganon, often disguising themselves as townsfolk in hopes of luring potential heroes to an unwitting death.
![Ache](https://i.imgur.com/vgsXRnF.png)
)

## Acheman ((++Acheman))
Monstrous bats cursed by evil. They are similar to aches, though they do not disguise themselves as Hylians like their counterparts. Instead, they hang from ceilings in deep red, ache-like forms. When their prey draws close, they swoop to the ground and transform into bat-like men that spit volleys of fire. After they spit a few blasts of flame, they return to their ache forms and return to the ceiling.

left(
# Giant Bats
The acheman is capable of transforming into an ache form or back into its monstrous humanoid form.

![Acheman](https://i.imgur.com/EQrrlKB.png)
)

# Aerocuda ((+Aerocuda))
An airborne creature that can be recognized by its distinctive cries. They have strong, dexterous feet and can often be seen cruising through the sky with animals or other monsters in their clutches. Thankfully, the breed's lightweight, aerodynamic body makes it easy to shoot down.

right(
# Monster Drop Troops
Aerocudas are commonly found holding blins and lizals in their grasps, swooping in and dropping them as a primitive form of drop troopers in war.

![Aerocuda](https://i.imgur.com/NJHVavD.png)
)

**HP** 15

**Dive Bomb** :a: **Frequency** once per round; **Effect** The aerocuda Flies in a straight line and makes a Strike at the end of that movement.

**Drop Object** :a: **Requirement** The aerocuda is holding an object; **Effect** The aerocuda Flies up to its fly Speed. At any point during this movement, it can drop an item of at least 1 bulk that it is carrying.  If the object is dropped on a creature, the creature takes 1d6 damage of the appropriate type for every 10 feet it has fallen with a maximum of 3d6 (DC 14 basic Reflex).

# Ampilus ((+Ampilus))
Ampilus are desert-dwelling animals, resembling a cross between a squilla and an ammonite, with an ability to internally generate electrical energy. Their shells are able to disperse weight surprisingly well, allowing them to safely traverse desert sinksand.

right(
# Quicksand Traversal
Ampilus shells have a weight-dispersing property that allows them to remain afloat on top of quicksand.  Shrewd adventurers can make use of this property to traverse areas blocked off by quicksand.

![Ampilus](https://i.imgur.com/x3B3C79.png)
)

item(
# Ampilus
## Creature 3
-
;N,Medium,Animal
**Perception** +9

**Skills** Athletics +10

**Str** +4, **Dex** +3, **Con** +3, **Int** -4, **Wis** +1, **Cha** +0

**Quicksand Immunity** The ampilus ignores difficult terrain caused by sand in deserts and does not trigger quicksand environmental hazards.
-
**AC** 19; **Fort** +9, **Ref** +7, **Will** +5

**HP** 48; **Immunities** electricity

**Electric Aura** (aura, electricity); **Requirement** The ampilus has withdrawn into its shell.  **Effect** 5 feet, 2d6 electricity damage, DC 18 basic Reflex save
-
**Speed** 25 feet

**Melee** :a: claw +12 (agile), **Damage** 1d6+5 slashing

**Shell Withdrawal** :a: The ampilus withdraws into its shell, which is charged with electricity.  While withdrawn into its shell, the ampilus's Speed increases by 10 feet as it rolls around, it gains an electric aura, and it cannot make a claw Strike but gains a slam Strike.  Its slam Strike has a +12 attack bonus, and deals 1d8+5 bludgeoning damage plus 1d6 electricity damage.
)

# Armos ((+Armos))

There are many kinds of ancient statues inside the various dungeons of Hyrule.  Some of these statues are capable of coming to life, hopping after the intruder that alerted them.  It is not known who built or animated these statues as there are a multitude of designs, not matching any one civilization.  The tiny Minish, for example, created some armos statues that they can pilot, but not all armos are capable of being piloted in this fashion.

## Armos
An armos appears indistinguishable from a stone statue, and in fact is comprised almost entirely of stone animated by magic. As a nonliving sentry, it remains dormant wherever its master or its creator has placed it. In many cases, an armos will stay on-guard for centuries or longer, remaining as motionless as the stone statue it resembles.

/

left(
# Ancient Guardians
Armos are usually found in ancient temples, standing silently and unmoving, coming to life only when an intruders walks near.

![Armos](https://i.imgur.com/f8IWw9Q.png)
)

item(
# Armos ((++Armos))
## Creature 3
-
;N,Medium,Armos,Construct,Mindless
**Perception** +6; darkvision

**Skills** Stealth +10

**Str** +4, **Dex** -2, **Con** +5, **Int** -5, **Wis** +0, **Cha** -5
-
**AC** 19 (15 when broken); **Fort** +12, **Ref** +5, **Will** +5; construct armor

**HP** 35; **Hardness** 6; **Immunities** bleed, death effects, disease, doomed, drained, fatigued, healing, mental, nonlethal attacks, paralyzed, poison, sickened, unconscious

**Construct Armor** Like normal objects, an armos has Hardness. This Hardness reduces any damage it takes by an amount equal to the Hardness. Once an armos is reduced to less than half its Hit Points, or immediately upon being damaged by a critical hit, its construct armor breaks and its Armor Class is reduced to 15.

**Death Burst** When an armos dies, its body explodes in a 5-foot aura of a concussive burst.  All creatures and objects in range take 3d6 sonic damage (DC 17 basic Reflex save).
-
**Speed** 20 feet

**Melee** :a: slam +11 (magical), **Damage** 1d8+6 bludgeoning
)
=
## Armos Knight
Larger variants of armos, these auto-homing statues were created to deter intruders. These variations will hop towards intruders much like their more standard brethren, but occasionally will stop suddenly to unleash spikes from their sides, when they will open their mouths.

## Armos Titan
A much larger armos statue built as a guardian for highly prized treasure or places of great importance. The armos titan uses its powerful fists in combat rather than a weapon, focusing on grappling its targets.

item(
# Armos Titan ((++Armos Titan))
## Creature 12
-
;Uncommon,N,Large,Armos,Construct,Mindless
**Perception** +20; darkvision

**Skills** Athletics +25, Stealth +25

**Str** +7, **Dex** +2, **Con** +7, **Int** -5, **Wis** +0, **Cha** -5
-
**AC** 33 (29 when broken); **Fort** +25, **Ref** +20, **Will** +19; construct armor

**HP** 200; **Hardness** 12; **Immunities** bleed, death effects, disease, doomed, drained, fatigued, healing, mental, nonlethal attacks, paralyzed, poison, sickened, unconscious

**Construct Armor** Like normal objects, an armos titan has Hardness. This Hardness reduces any damage it takes by an amount equal to the Hardness. Once an armos titan is reduced to less than half its Hit Points, or immediately upon being damaged by a critical hit, its construct armor breaks and its Armor Class is reduced to 29.

**Reactive Strike** :r:  When a creature triggers the armos titan's Reactive Strike, it can attempt an Athletics check to Grapple the triggering creature instead of making a melee Strike  It can still disrupt a triggering manipulate action if it critically succeeds at its attempt.
-
**Speed** 25 feet

**Melee** :a: fist +26 (magical, reach 10 feet), **Damage** 3d10+14 bludgeoning plus Grab

**Body Slam** :a: **Requirement** The armos titan has a creature grabbed; **Effect** The armos titan throws its foe against the ground. The grabbed creature takes 7d6 bludgeoning damage and is knocked prone. The grapple ends.

**Whirling Throw** :aa:  **Requirement** The armos titan has a creature grabbed; **Effect** The armos titan attempts to throw the grabbed creature.  The armos titan makes an Athletics check against the creature's Fortitude DC.
**Critical Success** The grabbed creature is thrown into a space within 30 feet, takes 8d6 bludgeoning damage, and is prone.  If the grabbed creature is thrown into another target creature, the target creature takes half this damage and is knocked prone.
**Success** As critical success except the creature is thrown into a space within 10 feet and takes 6d6 bludgeoning damage.
**Failure** The armos titan tosses the creature aside.  The grapple ends. The grabbed creature falls prone.
**Critical Failure** The armos titan loses hold of the creature and the grapple ends.
)

# Aruroda ((+Aruroda))

Large scorpion-like animals, aruroda are commonly found on beaches, in deserts, and inside caves. They prefer to nest under the sand and also use the sand as a way to hide and ambush any potential prey that comes nearby. Aruroda use their powerful venom to incapacitate prey and then drag the helpless creature underneath into the aruroda's nest to be feasted upon. They are capable of igniting their venom and firing small globs of ignited venom from their stinger, sometimes hiding under the sand with just the stinger exposed to stay out of sight while spraying ignited venom at potential threats.

/

right(
# Flammable Venom 
Aruroda venom is highly prized for its flammable properties, often being used in the creation of alchemist's fire or as a reagent for fire spells.

![Aruroda](https://i.imgur.com/WnkM1I7.png)
)

item(

**Skills** Athletics +12, Stealth +10

-
**AC** 20; **Fort** +14, **Ref** +8, **Will** +8

**HP** 63; **Weaknesses** vulnerable eye

**Vulnerable Eye** (vulnerability) A creature may take a -2 circumstance penalty to its attack to target the eye.  The auroda has weakness 10 to piercing damage and weakness 5 to other types of damage from Strikes that target the eye.
-
**Speed** 25 feet, burrow 10 feet

**Melee** :a: claw +12 (agile), **Damage** 2d6+5 piercing plus Grab

**Melee** :a: stinger +12 (reach 10 feet), **Damage** 2d8+5 piercing plus aruroda venom

)

# Baba ((+Baba))
A baba, more commonly known as deku baba, is a species of carnivorous plants, commonly found in deep forests.  Normally stationary, baba remain inactive until potential prey walks near, at which point the plant lunges forwards to attempt to devour the unlucky soul that wandered too close.

## Diababa ((++Diababa))
A diababa is an immense form of deku baba twisted by diaboloical magic, a cursed forest, or otther monstrous supernatural phenomenon.  In its evolved and utterly evil form, diababa exists to destroy.

left(
# Carnivorous Plants
Like the deku baba it evolved from, a diababa is a carnivorous plant, consuming animals and people that wander too close for nutrition.

![Diababa](https://i.imgur.com/ezSlhvX.png)
)

item(

**HP** 120; **Immunities** frightened, poison; **Resistances** acid 5, bludgeoning 5, slashing 5

**Lunge** :r: **Trigger** A creature within reach of the diababa's jaws uses a move action or leaves a square during a move action it's using.  **Effect** The diababa makes a jaws Strike at the creature with a -2 penalty.  If it hits, the diababa disrupts the creature's action.

**Melee** :a: jaws +17 (reach 15 feet), **Damage** 2d6+8 piercing plus Grab and Baba Poison

item(
# Bari
## Creature 4
-
;N,Medium,Amphibious,Animal,Mindless
**Perception** +11; darkvision

**Skills** Acrobatics +12

**Str** +1, **Dex** +3, **Con** +3, **Int** -5, **Wis** +0, **Cha** -2
-
**AC** 20; **Fort** +11, **Ref** +14, **Will** +6

**HP** 60; **Immunities** electricity, mental

**Bioelectrical Pulse** (aura, electricity) The bari pulses with electrical energy, discharging it when a threat comes near.  When an adjacent creature touches the biri or hits it with a physical attack, that creature takes 3d6 electricity damage unless it succeeds at a DC 21 Fortitude save.

**Split** When the bari is hit by an attack that would deal slashing or piercing damage and has 10 or more HP, it splits into two identical bari, each with half the original’s HP. One bari is in the same space as the original, and the other appears in an adjacent unoccupied space. If no adjacent space is unoccupied, it automatically pushes creatures and objects out of the way to fill a space (the GM decides if an object or creature is too big or sturdy to push).  A bari can only split once.
-
**Speed** 15 feet, swim 25 feet

**Melee** :a: tentacle +9 (electricity, reach 10 feet), **Damage** 1d8+1 bludgeoning plus 2d6 electricity

**Tentacle Spin** :aa: The bari spins in place, making a tentacle attack at each creature within reach.   The tentacle attacks count against the bari's multiple attack penalty, but don't apply the penalty until after all attacks have been made.
)
=
## Barinade ((++Barinade))
A large sea anenome-like monster, barinade are monstrous parasites that feed upon the life energy of larger creatures, such as Jabu-Jabu.  Barinade are able to absorb and channel the bioelectrical energy of the host, unleashing powerful beams of electrical energy as a defense mechanism.

right(
![Barinade](https://i.imgur.com/itWZROX.png)
)

item(
# Barinade
## Creature 7
-
;Rare,N,Large,Amphibious,Animal,Electricity
**Perception** +12; darkvision

**Skills** Athletics +15

**Str** +4, **Dex** +3, **Con** +4, **Int** -4, **Wis** +0, **Cha** -3
-
**AC** 24; **Fort** +18, **Ref** +14, **Will** +12

**HP** 144; **Immunities** electricity, precision; **Resistances** bludgeoning 10; **Weaknesses** piercing 5, slashing 5

**Bari Defense** Barinade has 6 bari defending its core.  Each bari can be targeted as a separate creature, with AC 22 and HP 12, though damaging them also reduces barinade's HP.  Each bari killed reduces the bludgeoning damage dealt by Bari Spin by 1d6.  As long as barinade still has a living bari connected to it, it can use Bari Spin.
-
**Speed** 25 feet, swim 25 feet

**Melee** :a: slam +18, **Damage** 2d8+8 bludgeoning

**Ranged** :a: bioelectrical beam +16 (electricity, range 30 feet), **Damage** 2d8+11 electricity

**Bari Spin** :aa: Barinade spins its bari around it while moving.  Barinade Strides and deals 6d6 bludgeoning plus 1d6 electricity damage (DC 25 basic Reflex save) to each creature it moves within 10 feet of during its stride.  A creature can only take this damage once per round.  The bludgeoning damage is reduced by 1d6 for each bari killed.  Barinade cannot use Bari Spin if all its bari have been killed.

**Charged Bioelectrical Beam** :aa: (electricity) Barinade unleashes a powerful beam of electricity in a 30-foot line that deals 6d8 electricity damage (DC 25 basic Reflex save).  Barinade cannot use Charged Electrical Beam again for 1d4 rounds.
)
=
# Blins ((+Blins))
A loose collection of monstrous humanoids with a common progenitor, the blin serve as rank-and-file soldiers for Ganon's armies. Nearly universally feared across Hyrule for their propensity to violence and brutal primitivism, the blin roam the wilderness - sometimes on direct orders from Ganon, and other times simply as hunters - making travel less safe as a result.

/
## Bokoblins ((++Bokoblins))

The second smallest and weakest of the blin tribes, the bokoblins make up for their size in large numbers. Not as cunning as the smaller miniblins, nor as strong as their moblin or bulblin brethren, bokoblins tend to act as cannon fodder in wartime or as common bandits led by a stronger moblin.

left(
# Blin Camps
Bokoblins are very common across Hyrule and often band together in camps, either lead by a larger moblin or a stronger blue or black bokoblin.

![Bokoblin](https://i.imgur.com/rhRikF9.png)
)

item (
# Bokoblin ((+++Bokoblin))
## Creature 1
-

## Technoblins ((+++Technoblin))
Bokoblins tend to use found scraps of technology in fights whenever they can. There are some that have found more useful bits of technology to fight with. These technoblins, as they are called, use swords that are electrified as well as more advanced armor to protect themselves.

right(
# Scavengers
Technoblins are intelligent enough to be able to use the ancient technology that they scavenge, though they do not understand the mechanisms of said technology.

![Technoblin](https://i.imgur.com/k7ZZ3nk.png)
)

**Critical Success** The creature is unaffected.
**Success** The creature is stunned 1.
**Failure** The creature is stunned 2.
**Critical Failure** The creature is stunned 3.

## Bokoblin Horde ((+++Bokoblin Horde))

Bokoblins are individually weak and so use their superior numbers to make up for their lack of strength.  A troop of bokoblins is usually led by a black, silver, or gold bokoblin.

item (
# Bokoblin Horde
## Creature 5
-
;CE,Gargantuan,Blin,Humanoid,Troop
**Perception** +12; low-light vision

**Languages** Blin

**Skills** Athletics +14, Intimidation +12, Survival +12

**Str** +5, **Dex** +2, **Con** +4, **Int** +0, **Wis** +2, **Cha** +2
-
**AC** 22; **Fort** +14, **Ref** +11, **Will** +11

**HP** 75 (16 squares); **Thresholds** 50 (12 squares), 25 (8 squares); **Weaknesses** area damage 10, splash damage 5

**Troop Defenses**
-
**Speed** 25 feet; troop movement

**Arrow Volley** :aa: The bokoblins draw or reload their shortbows and launch a ranged attack in the form of a volley.  This volley is a 10-foot burst within 60 feet that deals 3d6+3 piercing damage (DC 19 basic Reflex save).  When the bokoblins are reduced to 8 or fewer squares, this area decreases to a 5-foot burst.

**Charge!** :aa: **Requirements** the horde has Formed Up; **Effect** The bokoblins lower their spears and charge.  The troop Strides in a straight line until they're adjacent to an enemy then use Lower Spears!, dealing 1d8+11 piercing damage.  Any creature that fails its save is also knocked prone.

**Form Up** :a:

**Lower Spears!** :a: to :aaa: **Frequency** once per round; **Effect** The bokoblins engage in a coordinated spear attack against each enemy within 10 feet, with a DC 19 basic Reflex save.  The damage depends on the number of actions.
:a: 1d8 piercing damage
:aa: 1d8+8 piercing damage
:aaa: 1d8+11 piercing damage

**Troop Movement** Whenever the bokoblins Stride, they first Form Up as a free action to condense into a 20-foot-by-20-foot area (minus any missing squares), the move up to their Speed.  This works just like a Gargantuan creature moving; for instance, if any square of the bokoblins enter difficult terrain, the extra movement cost applies to all the bokoblins.
)
=

# Silver Bokoblin
## Creature 7
-
;Uncommon,CE,Medium,Blin,Humanoid
**Perception** +15; low-light vision

**Languages** Blin

**Skills** Acrobatics +15, Athletics +17, Intimidation +15, Survival +15

**Str** +5, **Dex** +5, **Con** +4, **Int** +2, **Wis** +3, **Cha** +2

**Items** *+1* greatclub, composite shortbow (20 arrows)
-
**AC** 24; **Fort** +15, **Ref** +18, **Will** +12

**HP** 115
-
**Speed** 25 feet

**Melee** :a: greatclub +18 (backswing, magical, shove), **Damage** 2d10+9 bludgeoning

**Ranged** :a: composite shortbow +16 (brutal, deadly 1d10, propulsive, range increment 60 feet, reload 0), **Damage** 2d6+9 piercing

**Club Critical Specialization** On a critical hit, the target of the critical hit is shoved up to 10 feet away from the bokoblin.

**Incessant Taunting** :a: The silver bokoblin uses rude gestures and mocking dances to attempt to goad their enemies into attacking them.  It attempts an Intimidation check against the Will DC of a single creature within 30 feet.
**Critical Success** The target is off-guard for 1 round. On its next turn, if the bokoblin are within the target's reach, the target must spend at least two actions attacking the bokoblin before it can act freely.
**Success** As critical success, except the target only needs to spend one action attacking the bokoblin.
**Failure** The target is unaffected.
**Critical Failure** The target is unaffected and is temporarily immune to Incessant Taunting for 1 hour.
)

## Horriblins ((++Horriblins))
Horriblins are blins that cling to the ceilings of dark places such as caves.  They are known for their large, bulbous noses, gray skin, and hammer-shaped horns.  They often attack using spears and by throwing boulders that they tear out of the environment.

## Miniblins ((++Miniblins))

An adult miniblin stands at a height comparable to a small hylian child, with facial features reminiscent of a mouse. These creatures are known for both the bizarrely unique chirping and giggling noises they make, and their uncanny ability to ascend even the smoothest of walls with ease. Like most moblins, a miniblin's coloration varies from one to the next, with reds and browns being the most abundant.

left(
# Aquatic Miniblins
Some miniblins almost exclusively live out at sea.  They are usually identified by having small fins and are often seen wearing goggles.

![Miniblin](https://i.imgur.com/7FdOGtt.png)

You can represent an aquatic miniblin by giving the normal miniblin a swim speed of 20 feet.
)

item (

## Moblins ((++Moblins))
Also known as big blins, brown moblins, or occasionally mudblins, these brown-skinned creatures are often considered icons of their race. A typical adult moblin towers most other humanoids, with over 8 feet of muscle and fat - a gruesome and intimidating sight that earns its title of "big." Although they usually live in wilderness among beasts, big moblins are generally apex predators in their environment. They have been known to populate almost any terrestrial landscape, but prefer temperate climates with abundant fauna due to their carnivorous diet.

left(
![Moblin](https://i.imgur.com/tRz7HAJ.png)
)

## Shield Moblin ((+++Shield Moblin))
Moblins that appear as corpulent red monsters twice the size of the average hylian. Their brute strength, powerful spears, and durable shields they carry makes them considerably dangerous enemies. When disarmed of their shield, these moblins fly into a rage making them even more formidable.

left(
![Shield Moblin](https://i.imgur.com/x2BBOS6.png)
)

**Spinning Spear** :aa: The moblin spins in place with its spear out.  The moblin makes up to four spear Strikes that deal slashing damage.  No single creature can be targeted by more than one spear Strike during one use of this ability.  These attacks count toward the moblin's multiple attack penalty, but the multiple attack penalty doesn't increase until after all the attacks are made.
)

## Great Moblin Mauler ((+++Great Moblin Mauler))
A moblin that has grown even larger from the nutrients of the forest will become a massive great moblin. Instead of charging with a large spear, great moblins favor using a maul that they can smash into the ground to unleash a large shockwave at intruders into their lairs. They are not very common, usually only one or two are seen in an entire tribe of forest moblins.

left(
![Great Moblin Mauler](https://i.imgur.com/444yfzK.png)
)

item (
# Great Moblin Mauler

# Boe ((+Boe))
Boes are shuffling, hazy balls that often thrive in the darkness, though a white variant exists that thrives in snow and bright lights instead.  Both types are not very threatening when isolated, and can be dispelled easily with a single attack. However, these floating creatures tend to cluster in groups, and in such situations can pose more of a threat to inexperienced adventurers.

left(
# Snow Variants
Most boes are black in color, but there exists a white variant that lives in snowy regions rather than places of darkness.  White boes have a bonus to Stealth in snowy conditions instead of darkness.

# Bubble ((+Bubble))

The bubble is a flying skull with blue flames and the deadly ability to jinx creatures who are unfortunate enough to be caught up in the flames. Those jinxed by a bubble find themselves afflicted with a curse that prevents them from fighting back, though wise adventurers always bring a shield to help extinguish the occult flames.

left(
# Skull Camouflage
Bubbles disguise themselves as the skulls of corpses in the dungeons that they inhabit, coming to life when a creature comes near.

![Bubble](https://i.imgur.com/pudngcG.png)
)

**Critical Success** The creature is unaffected and is temporarily immune to the blue flame aura for 1 hour.
**Success** The creature is unaffected and is temporarily immune to the blue flame aura for 1 minute.
**Failure** The creature cannot use an action with the attack trait until the end of its next turn.

# Lord Bullbo ((++Lord Bullbo))
An extremely large bullbo and favored mount of King Bulblin.  It has horns that grow from just behind its eyes instead of the standard Bullbo's tusks. Lord Bullbo's horns are not completely white as common bullbo' tusks are. Instead, they are striped red and white and are much larger. Lord Bullbo's roar is also pitched much lower than a normal bullbo's, likely due to its size. Since Lord Bullbo is extremely large, it is also immensely strong and can easily fling smaller creatures out of the way with its horns.

# Chuchus ((+Chuchus))
Chuchus, sometimes known as chus, are gelatinous creatures of living slime or jelly, often depicted with facial features.  They can become elementally charged, with some chuchus being charged with fire, electricity, or ice powers.

## Muck Chuchu ((++Muck Chuchu))
Muck chuchus are found in areas defiled by waste, generally known as muck by the zora.  Evil forces tend to generate the muck that spawns muck chuchus in dark areas filled with water.

item(
# Muck Chuchu

;N,Medium,Chuchu,Mindless,Ooze

**AC** 8; **Fort** +9, **Ref** +1, **Will** +3

-
**Speed** 10 feet

**Muck Wave** :a: **Frequency** once per minute; **Effect** The muck chuchu unleashes a wave of muck, covering all creatures within a 20-foot emanation. Each creature in the area must succeed at a DC 17 Reflex save or take 1d4 acid damage and take a -10-foot penalty to its Speeds for 1 minute (on a critical failure, the creature also falls prone). A creature can spend and Interact action to clean someone off, decreasing the Speed penalty by 5 feet with each action.
)

## Volatile Chuchu ((++Volatile Chuchu))
Some chuchus are elementally unstable.  When exposed to cold, electricity, or fire, this kind of chuchu is able to change its composition to become charged with that same kind of energy.

# Colgera ((+Colgera))
A massive insectoid monster with a long sinuous body studded with icy spikes, capable of harnessing both wind and cold to bring about powerful blizzards.  Colgera is found high in the sky, feasting on the few high-flying creatures and rarely coming down to the surface; however, there are rare reports of the beast appearing in the Depths, the massive underground cavern that spans the breadth of Hyrule.

left(
# Scourge of the Skies
Colgera rarely comes down to the surface, but those who dwell in the skies are at risk of a colgera attack.

![Colgera](https://i.imgur.com/GG21XeW.png)
)

item(
# Colgera
## Creature 8
-
;Rare, NE, Gargantuan, Air, Beast, Cold
**Perception** +16; low-light vision, snow vision

**Skills** Acrobatics +16, Athletics +18, Stealth +14

**Str** +6, **Dex** +3, **Con** +4, **Int** -3, **Wis** +4, **Charisma** +2

**Snow Vision** Snow doesn't impair Colgera's vision; it ignores concealment from snowfall.
-
**AC** 25; **Fort** +19, **Ref** +14, **Will** +16

**HP** 170; **Immunities** cold; **Weaknesses** fire 8; vulnerable underside

**Vulnerable Underside** (vulnerability) Colgera has three glowing spots on its underside, each frosted over with a thick carapace of ice that has Hardness 8.  A creature may take a -2 circumstance penalty to its attack to target one of these glowing spots.  Colgera has weakness 10 to piercing damage that penetrates the Hardness of the carapace.  Fire damage melts the carapace entirely, enabling attacks to target the glowing spot directly without having to overcome Hardness.

**Wounded Fury** When Colgera is reduced to half health, it regenerates any broken carapaces from its Vulnerable Underside and can use its Terrible Tornadoes.
-
**Speed** fly 50 feet

**Melee** :a: jaws +20 (reach 15 feet) **Damage** 2d10+11 piercing

**Ranged** :a: spikes +18 (cold, range increment 60 feet) **Damage** 2d8+6 piercing plus 1d6 cold

**Dimensional Portal** :aa: (move, primal, teleportation) Colgera opens a dimensional portal and enters it, exiting at a spot of its choosing within 300 feet.

**Skyward Spikes** :aa: Colgera makes three Strikes with its spikes, each at a -2 penalty and targeting a different creature.  These Strikes count as only 1 attack for Colgera, and the penalty doesn't increase until after it has made all 3 attacks.
)
=
item(
**Terrible Tornadoes** :aa: (air, cold, primal) **Requirement** Colgera has been reduced to half health or lower.  **Effect** Colgera summons three tornadoes within 50 feet, each a cylinder with a 15-foot radius and 120 feet tall.  All squares within the tornadoes are difficult terrain. All creatures in the area take 3d10 bludgeoning damage and 3d10 cold damage as powerful freezing winds buffet them, with a DC 26 Reflex save.  A creature can be affected by the tornadoes only once per round.  The tornadoes last for 3 rounds.  Colgera can't use Terrible Tornadoes again for 1d4 rounds.  If Colgera summons more tornadoes while the previous set of tornadoes are still active, the previous set disappears.
**Critical Success** The creature is unaffected.
**Success** The creature takes half damage.
**Failure** The creature takes full damage and rises 10 feet into the air. If it doesn't have a fly Speed, the creature gains one equal to its Speed until it either reaches the ground or ceases to be in the whirlwind's area, potentially falling when the spell ends or when it leaves the area.
**Critical Failure** As failure, except the creature takes double damage and rises 20 feet into the air.

**The Serpent Below** :aaa: Colgera roars and disappears into a portal, only to reappear seconds later making a charge.  Colgera uses Dimensional Portal, then Flies up to twice its fly Speed and makes a jaws Strike.
)

# Dead Hand ((+Dead Hand))
A dead hand has a zombie-like head with a large jaw. Its blood is a green color, and red blotches, thought to be bloodstains, cover its body. Multiple seemingly disembodied hands circle the chamber in which the dead hand resides. The creature uses these hands to snag prey, at which point its main body emerges from the ground to consume the captured meal.

left(
# Lair of Hands
A dead hand's lair typically is an empty room with several of its hands poking up from beneath the ground, with the main body remaining underground and out of sight until prey has been captured.

# Deku Scrub ((+Deku Scrub))
Deku scrubs are plant-based creatures that have skin made of wood and hair and "clothing" made of leaves and flowers, and spit deku nuts at their enemies when threatened. They usually appear in a small, flower-like tuft of foliage which they hide within when threatened. They often appear as enemies, but despite their antagonistic nature they tend to be friendly, at least when they believe it to be to their own benefit. It is rumored that a deku scrub's disposition can change drastically depending on the type of tree they are born from.

## Business Scrub ((++Business Scrub))
Some deku scrubs take up jobs as merchants, wandering the world to peddle their wares.  They are cowardly by nature, preferring to hide in their flowers instead of fight.

left(
![Business Scrub](https://i.imgur.com/ihSS3HU.png)
)

## Mad Scrub ((++Mad Scrub))
Much more aggressive than common deku scrubs, mad scrubs attack any creatures that draw near with the intent to kill. After all, a corpse will eventually provide extra nourishment to the deku flower the mad scrub calls home. They distrust any and all who would approach them, save occasionally other deku scrubs. Mad scrubs can be found anywhere where flora is abundant, but are most common in marshes and wetlands.

/
left(
# Madness
A mad scrub's madness overtakes any previous reason they once had, leaving them to be forsaken by other Deku and banished to live a lonely life away from civilization.

![Mad Scrub](https://i.imgur.com/0UdX6wU.png)
)

# Devalant ((+Devalant))
Devalants are giant, burrowing insects that dwell in desert regions.  They create sinkholes in the sand as they burrow underneath, drawing in their prey.

right(
# Red and Blue
Devalants come in two general colors: red and blue.  Blue devalants are unable to spit fire like their red cousins.

A blue devalant can be represented by a devalant with the Weak adjustment and removing the fire spit attack.
![Devalant](https://i.imgur.com/pmEYQxx.png)
)

**Pull Under** :aa: **Requirement** The devalant is grabbing a creature.  **Effect** The devalant attempts to pull the creature under the sand. The devalant rolls an Athletics check against the creature's Fortitude DC. On a success, the devalant pulls the creature under the sands. A creature pulled under the sands begins to suffocate. The creature can attempt a DC 18 Athletics check to break free of the devalant and raise itself back up to the surface.

# Dodongo ((+Dodongo))
Dodongos are dinosaur-like reptiles that can grow to tremendous sizes. Most of them wield fire breath, immense physical strength, and thick armor-like scales. This combined with their feral aggression make them infamous monsters across the entire Light World. They have a notorious weakness to the thunderous detonations produced by bombs, and are almost single-handedly the reason any worthy adventurer keeps at least a few explosives at the ready. 

## Baby Dodongo ((++Baby Dodongo))
The infantile form of dodongos, baby dodongos are prone to exploding when killed. Despite being very young, they still have a nasty bite. They are small, serpentine creatures that slither along the ground, and burrow underneath for protection and ambushing.

left(
![Baby Dodongo](https://i.imgur.com/wHSB9hx.png)
)

**Death Throes** When the dodongo dies, its body explodes in a 5-foot burst of a fiery blast that deals 1d6 fire damage to each creature in the area (DC 14 basic Reflex save).

**AC** 15; **Fort** +6, **Ref** +8, **Will** +3

**HP** 15

## Kodongo ((++Kodongo))
A diminutive form of dodongo, kodongos are simple reptilian quadrupeds with a ravenous appetite. They are usually of either a red or green color, and bear some resemblance to unusually small rhinoceroses or triceratops. Kodongos dwell primarily in caves, ruins, and other dark locations, usually in small family-like packs. Kodongos spit blasts of magical flame at virtually anything that moves, with the apparent intent of roasting it alive and eating what remains—even if they aren't hungry. These beasts are believed to have been evolved to be impervious to heat just so their kind doesn't constantly roast and eat each other.

right(
# Flamespitters
Unlike larger dodongos, a kodongo is only capable of spitting out a small mote of flame from its maw rather than sweeping fire.

![Kodongo](https://i.imgur.com/ygCD3NL.png)

## Young Dodongo ((++Young Dodongo))
A young dodongo is a baby dodongo that has grown but not yet reached reproductive maturity. Although it is the equivalent of a child and hasn't even fully developed mobile limbs, this monster's fangs and fire breath are more than capable of ripping and roasting the most formidable of creatures. Despite being relatively slow and clumsy for its size, this dodongo hunts endlessly to spur its growth into adulthood. Relatively few young dodongos thrive into the next stage of their life cycle, the king dodongo.

left(
# Hungry Prowlers
Young dodongos often prowl the caverns where the dodongo brood lives, searching for any kind of prey to feast upon.

![Young Dodongo](https://i.imgur.com/0LIvEL7.png)
)

## Gecko Dodongo ((++Gecko Dodongo))
Dodongos that are adapted to smaller caves and have feet that allow them to stick to the sides of walls and ceilings like a gecko would, hence the name gecko dodongo. Gecko dodongos are not nearly as large as their other brethren, but they are no less deadly. They share the same weakness to bombs that other dodongos do, though their hide is not nearly as tough.

## King Dodongo ((++King Dodongo))
A rare baby dodongo is able to live into adolescence to become a young dodongo, and a rare young is able to thrive into full adulthood as a king. Fitting to its name, a king dodongo is usually the apex predator in whatever caverns or ruins it seeks to dominate. Its lair is often filled with younger dodongos who both serve their parent: the king. These younglings are protected by the sheer presence of the king itself, as its roars and utter power are known to clear almost any other creatures that would bring harm its offspring.

left(
# Hail to the King
Other dodongos rarely challenge the authority of the king dodongo, remaining subservient and in the young dodongo stage of their life.  In the rare event that two king dodongos develop in the same brood, the two kings will fight each other for control of the territory to the death or until one leaves to find a different area to raise a brood.

![King Dodongo](https://i.imgur.com/qISkwkf.png)
)

## Dongorongo ((++Dongorongo))

A dodongo-like creature, the dongorongo resembles a large armored lizard with crystals growing out of its back. Like a dodongo, it is vulnerable to explosives going off inside its body. Some speculate that the dongorongo is an evolved form of the dodongo, others say it is a magically enhanced dodongo. Either way, a dongorongo is a force to deal with in their homes deep inside volcanic mountains.

left(
# Pure Metal
Dongorongo are found near deposits of a special material known as Crimsonine, one of the Pure Metals used to forge the Phantom Sword.  The crystals in a dongorongo's back are speculated to be this material.

![Young Dodongo](https://i.imgur.com/YrzXwV8.png)
)

# Dragons ((+Dragons))

## Aquamentus ((++Aquamentus))
As large green-colored dragons, any aquamentus is a rare but terrifying monster. Warriors can rarely even do it harm unless they strike the creature's singular horn, the source of the dragon's magical prowess. Such a task would be difficult on its own, let alone with the monster blasting out magical flames at any would-be foes.  Despite its prowess, a typical aquamentus is more of a beast than a warlock—it lacks the cunning for well-thought out plans or long-term goals, despite its longevity as a dragon.


right(
# Magical Hoarder
An aquamentus has an inherent, instinctive desire to find and hoard that which is magical. These rare creatures are known to kill adventurers for their magic items, and drag the trinkets away into some secretive lair in cave or ruins.

Typical loot found in an aquamentus's hoard include a +1 weapon and a number of talismans with combined level up to level 5.
![Aquamentus](https://i.imgur.com/Yj4RF4Z.png)
)

## Argorok ((++Argorok))

A large red dragon that is often found covered in black armor, argoroks are a fearsome sight in the skies. They usually keep to themselves high above the clouds, but powerful sorcerers have been known to control them with dark magic to do their bidding. Despite their prowess, an argorok is not especially intelligent, barely able to understand others during the rare times it is not aggressive.
/

left(
# Twilit Dragon
Ancient Twili magic has been known to control argoroks, leading to argoroks being colloqually known as Twilit Dragons.

## Blizzagia ((++Blizzagia))
left(
![Blizzagia](https://i.imgur.com/jIXeWl7.png)
)

Blizzagia appear as colossal, blue-colored, burrowing serpents roughly 60 feet in length. They have a backside covered in crystalline blue spines, and faces covered in a brown-colored helmet-like mask for protection. Its razor-sharp, snake-like fangs are larger than even the longest spears.  Any blizzagia can live for centuries, and is often the apex predator in whatever frigid climate it calls home. One typically dwells in a burrow several stories below the ground's surface, where it rests the vast majority of the time. A blizzagia usually only leaves its burrow in rare instances to hunt, but when it does it can devour an entire village before it is satisfied.
/

The blizzagia's coils can hold as many creatures as will fit in its space.

# Gleeok ((++Gleeok))
Gleeoks are multiheaded dragons that terrorize the wilderness and dungeons.  They normally can be found with two, three, or four heads but there are rare sightings of gleeoks with more heads than these.

## Flame Gleeok ((+++Flame Gleeok))
Flame gleeoks are three-headed, winged gleeoks.  They are massive creatures, towering well above and even dwarfing other large enemies such as molduga.  Flaming horns grow out of the top of their heads, and each head bears a single eyeball.  Each head can shoot fireballs and streams of fire separately, as well as all at once.  Their large wings allow them to hover above the ground; when at low health, they fly high into the air and unleash massive fireballs.

right(
![Flame Gleeok](https://i.imgur.com/MoIhT10.png)
)

item(
# Flame Gleeok
## Creature 8
-
;NE,Uncommon,Gargantuan,Dragon,Fire,Gleeok
**Perception** +16; darkvision

**Languages** Hylian, Lizal

**Skills** Acrobatics +15, Athletics +19, Intimidation +16

**Str** +5, **Dex** +3, **Con** +4, **Int** -2, **Wis** +3, **Cha** +4
-
**AC** 27; **Fort** +17, **Ref** +16, **Will** +16; +1 status to all saves vs. magic; all-around vision

**HP** 150 (body); **Immunities** fire, paralysis, sleep; **Weaknesses** cold 10

**HP** 50 (head); **Immunities** area damage; **Weaknesses** slashing 5

**Multiple Heads** The gleeok has three heads.  A creature can attempt to sever one of the gleeok's heads by specifically targeting it and dealing damage equal to the head's Hit Points. A head that is not completely severed returns to full Hit Points at the end of any creature's turn.  If all three heads are destroyed, the gleeok dies.

**Multiple Opportunities** A gleeok gains an extra reaction per round for each of its heads beyond the first, which it can use only to make Reactive Strikes.  It can't use more than 1 reaction on the same triggering action, even if a creature leaves several squares within its reach, and the gleeok must use a different head for each Reactive Strike it makes.  Whenever one of the gleeok's heads is severed, the gleeok loses 1 of its extra reactions per round.

**Reactive Strike** :r:
-
**Speed** 30 feet, fly 60 feet

**Melee** :a: jaws +20 (fire, magical, reach 20 feet), **Damage** 2d10+10 piercing plus 2d6 fire

**Melee** :a: claw +20 (agile, magical, reach 15 feet), **Damage** 2d10+10 slashing

**Melee** :a: tail +18 (magical, reach 25 feet), **Damage** 2d8+10 bludgeoning

**Breath Weapon** :aa: (arcane, fire) The gleeok breathes fire that deals 9d6 fire damage in its choice of a 30-foot burst within 100 feet or a 60-foot cone (DC 26 basic Reflex save).  If firing a cone, the gleeok can use its Breath Weapon a number of times equal to the number of heads it has.  It can't use Breath Weapon again for 1d4 rounds.
)
=
item(
**Focused Assault** :aa: The gleeok attacks a single target with its heads, overwhelming its foe with multiple attacks and leaving almost nowhere to dodge.  The gleeok Strikes with its jaws.  On a successful attack, the gleeok deals damage from its jaws Strike to the target, plus an additional 1d6 damage for every head it has beyond the first.  Even on a failed attack, the gleeok deals the damage from one jaws Strike to the target creature, though it still misses completely on a critical failure.  This counts toward the gleeok's multiple attack penalty as a number of attacks equal to the number of heads the gleeok has.

**Gleeok Momentum** The gleeok recharges its Breath Weapon whenever it scores a critical hit with a Strike.

**Storm of Jaws** :aa:  The gleeok makes a number of Strikes up to its number of heads, each against a different target. These attacks count toward the gleeok's multiple attack penalty, but the multiple attack penalty doesn't increase until after the gleeok makes all its attacks.

**Wing Buffet** :aa:  The gleeok attempts to buffet away all creatures within 20 feet of it using its wings.  The gleeok makes a single Athletics check to Shove, comparing the result to the Fortitude DCs of all targets.
)

Moragia is an enormous monster dwelling in Death Mountain.  Its body is composed of boiling lava and hard rocks that are infused with gloom, a concentrated form of malice. ## Volvagia ((++Volvagia))

Volvagia is the name given to an ancient serpentine dragon that lives in the depths of Death Mountain and was essentially the spirit of the mountain. It is said that a legendary Goron destroyed it with the use of the Megaton Hammer, but Ganondorf used dark magic to resurrect the dragon to secure the Fire Temple. Volvagia was fed gorons as an example to the other races.

# Dragonfly of Termina ((+Dragonfly of Termina))
Although dragonflies across most of the world are tiny and relatively docile, those in Termina are infamous for their aggression and freakishly large size. An adult is typically the size of a pony. Inherently carnivorous, these soaring insects hunt down prey as large and robust as hylians and zora thanks to a massive stinger that crackles with electricity. Like smaller dragonflies, these monsters can be found in many diverse environments, but tend towards marshes or other areas of abundant freshwater.

![Dragonfly of Termina](https://i.imgur.com/BF1aOPo.png)

# Elementals ((+Elementals))

## Chilfos ((++Chilfos))
Chilfos are warriors that appear to consist of animated bones made of ice.  Chilfos are capable of forming icicle spears by forcibly condensing water vapor in the air, which they use to attack in both melee and at range by throwing the spear at enemies.  Those struck by a chilfos's spear are afflicted with a spreading coldness as the magic that animates the chilfos seeps into their body.

left(

)
Appearing as a large molten rock cyclops, Cragma, the Lava Lord, is a guardian of temples devoted to fire and earth.  Cragma fights in a brutish manner, not caring much for advanced tactics and strategy and instead uses his immense strength to smash his enemies.  He prefers to fight in caverns or similar environments with easy access to lava as he is capable of rending the very earth itself with his attacks, causing immense environmental damage.

**Toss** :a: **Requirement** Cragma has a creature Grabbed. **Effect** Cragma hurls the creature up to 50 feet at a wall or the ground.  The thrown creature takes 3d6+11 bludgeoning damage (DC 33 basic Fortitude save) and lands prone.

## Eeno ((++Eeno))

From a distance, an eeno appears indistinguishable from a lumpy pile of snow, and is rarely found not among snow or ice. Its body is in fact almost entirely snow. When agitated, an eeno's body forms a face with glowing yellow eyes to see, and large arms—though it lacks legs, and still mostly takes the form of a snow pile. It wildly attacks any foreign creatures that enter its territory, usually with powerfully-hurled packs of snow or ice it has gathered from the surrounding environment. When all else fails, it will either flee into the depths of snow, or resort to crude but powerful punches.

/

**Ice Walk** The freezard ignores difficult terrain and greater difficult terrain from ice and snow and doesn't risk falling when crossing ice.

=
## Geldman ((++Geldman))

Sometimes referred to as a "sandman," a geldman appears as a massive, powerfully-built humanoid about 10 feet in height. Its body seems to be composed entirely of tightly-packed sand, save for the stark white and pupil-devoid eyes that adorn its angered face. These monsters dwell almost exclusively in areas of loose sand, such as deserts or beaches, where they spend most of their time just under the surface of the sand. When a foreign creature approaches, the geldman manifests its powerful upper body above the sand, and rapidly "wades" through the dunes towards the intruder. For seemingly for no purpose other than pure cruelty and malice, a geldman attacks with powerful punches from fists as hard as stone.

/
left(

Tales tell of a geldman grabbing unsuspecting travelers and pulling them deep under the dunes to suffocate or starve in an agonizing death.

The geldman rolls an Athletics check against the creature's Fortitude DC. On a success, the geldman pulls the creature under the sands, and if it critically succeeds it can also make a fist Strike against the creature after the pull.  A creature pulled under the sands begins to suffocate.  The creature can attempt a DC 20 Athletics check to break free of the geldman and raise itself back up to the surface.

**Sand Burrow** The geldman can only use its burrow speed in sand.
)
=
## Heedle ((++Heedle))
A heedle is squat quadruped with a short tail, and glowing pupil-less white eyes that glow from within a solid stone mask that serves as its face. One can grow up to 10 feet in length. Any heedle almost constantly glows with smoldering ember, and its body appears as though it was composed of molten rock. Much like actual rock, it is virtually impenetrable to conventional forms of attack.

Heedles are often found in small groups of two or three, where they ravenously spread heat and flame across everything in their path. A heedle's existence seems only to serve to burn that which can burn, and it is only hostile towards those who would hinder this endless quest to ignite and scorch all that exists.

/

right(

A heedle leaves behind a path of fire where it treads, making it dangerous to wander in the same region as the heedle.

# Talus ((++Talus))
Taluses appear as a cluster of boulders at first, but once approached, they assemble into large golem-like beings.  Luminous, frost, and igneo variations can be found all around Hyrule.  A talus is very slow-moving but powerful, using a combination of punches, body slams, and launching rocks at those that disturb their resting spots or wander too close.

## Stone Pebblit ((+++Stone Pebblit))
A very young stone talus. Their bodies toughen as they mature, becoming as tough as boulders by adulthood. As a child, however, their bodies are light enough to be lifted and fragile enough to break when thrown.

# Frox ((+Frox))
A frox is a large frog-like animal with ores on its back and a singular eye, found in the Depths of Hyrule.  They typically attack with powerful leaps and by sucking everything in front of them into their gaping maws.

## Little Frox ((++Little Frox))
Little froxes are the juvenile form of froxes, very small compared to their adult brethren. Their powerful legs allow them to leap at potential prey and threats when they spot one.  They are typically found in groups of at least four.  Little froxes have a diet that consists of brightbloom seeds and ores.

# Gerudo ((+Gerudo))
Gerudo bear a strong resemblance to the more abundant hylian race. Gerudo however are of a uniformly darker skin tone, and always have red hair. Their eyes are usually golden, but are occasionally more exotic colors such as blue-green or violet. A typical female Gerudo stands over 6 feet tall. They are particularly muscular, but this may be more of a cultural difference than a physiological one, as gerudo prize athletes and warrior elites.

Perhaps the most characteristic aspect of gerudo, however, is that they are almost universally female.
/
## Gerudo Bandit ((++Gerudo Bandit))
Gerudo who have been banished from their communities tend to turn to banditry to survive the harshness of the desert.  Travelers in the desert must be wary of passing by large sand dunes as gerudo bandits make use of them to hide in for an ambush.

# Ghini ((+Ghini))
Ghini are one-eyed spirits that are normally found in graveyards, often depicted with their tongues lolling out of their mouths. They use this tongue to absorb the life force of people who wander into graveyards and disturb their resting places. A ghini has a ghostly tail it can extend to wrap around a person to immobilize them before licking their life force away.

# Gohma ((+Gohma))

## Gohma Larva ((++Gohma Larva))
A gohma larva—or "baby gohma"—is a newborn offspring of an infamous monster called gohma. Like its mother, a larva is an spider-like creature, but only has two to four functional legs. It peers upon the world with a single eye, and generally seeks the violent destruction of anything not of its own kind. The exact dimensions and capabilities of a gohma larva depend slightly on the capabilities of its mother, but it tends to leap towards its victims with its fangs or slamming its whole body. As gohma eggs are produced in groups, larvae learn to function in small groups of their siblings or peers.

## Gohma ((++Gohma))
Bearing physiological similarities to both a spider and a crab, the colossal predatory monster known as gohma spans almost 10 feet across. It bears four or six functional legs capable of climbing almost any surface. A gohma's entire body is plated in chitin more dense than iron that protects it from virtually all forms of conventional attack, save for its single imposing eye.

## Fire Gohma ((++Fire Gohma))
Nearly a hundred feet long, a fire gohma is nearly the size of a mountain. Its colossal centipede-like body is layered entirely with incredibly thick chitin reminiscent of mammalian bones. The rare cracks in this natural armor reveal an interior body that glows with searing heat. Its large, singular eye is the only portion of its body left entirely unarmored. True to its name, a fire gohma literally lives and swims in subterranean flows of molten rock, and subsists in part on heat. In the rare instances it surfaces, entire towns can be left roasted by its breath, and age-old trees torn in half by its gargantuan pincer-like claws.

# Goron ((+Goron))
A race of rock people inhabiting Hyrule, Termina, and several other countries, typically living in mountain ranges.  Gorons have been called "rock people" since ancient times, when the goddess Hylia ruled and have long held close ties with the Hyrulean royal family.  They have the capability to thrive in any environment, and in times of crisis, have survived by migrating to different climes.  Befitting with that of their habitat, their durable, round bodies greatly resemble that of stones and boulders, and nearly all Gorons have a hide of ridged stones on their backsides. They usually have light brown skin. They have small eyes and noticeable lips, which conceal unaligned, square teeth.

Gorons possess immense strength which many are proud of, and many groups of Gorons like to hold competitions that test each other's physical strength and even rolling ability, including competitions such as sumo wrestling and rolling racing, among others.  While Gorons do have many strengths, they are also not without their weaknesses.  Gorons tend to move slowly, though their ability to roll can make up for this, and one of their apparent weaknesses is deep water as they cannot swim.  However, Gorons can hold their breath for long periods without ever needing to breathe and thus cannot drown.

## Goron Brawler ((++Goron Brawler))

## Fyrus ((++Fyrus))
A powerful Goron hero and chieftain who became corrupted by the powers of the Fused Shadow, becoming the beast known as Fyrus.  Fyrus is a mighty being of flame, capable of destruction on a large scale.  Fearing the destruction he could cause in this state, the Gorons of Death Mountain locked Fyrus away deep in the mountain where he remained until one could free him from his fate.

# Guardian ((+Guardian))
Ancient machines created by the Sheikah, originally created to aid in the battle against the calamity of Ganon.  However, the power of Ganon's malice was enough to overcome the programming of these machines, subverting many of them to his will.  Now, guardians are aggressors instead of protectors of the people they were built to protect.  Some guardians were spared from the malice, usually the scouts found in various shrines hidden throughout Hyrule.

## Guardian Scout ((++Guardian Scout))
left(
![Guardian Scout](https://i.imgur.com/TPzmJjK.png)
)

Guardian scouts are smaller variants of guardian stalkers, built for dual purpose of defense and as training tools.  They have been used as opponents in various trials devised by the Sheikah.  In addition to the beam functionality, guardian scouts are designed to handle weaponry as a means of further testing the combat prowess of one undertaking the trials.  It takes some serious skill to go toe-to-toe with one.

# Hinox ((+Hinox))

Cyclops-like ogres that have an affinity for bombs and commonly use them as weapons. Hinoxes typically appear as musclebound, light brown or red humanoids with a single eye. # Hylian ((+Hylian))
The most populous ancestry in Hyrule and its parallel counterparts Termina and Lorule, hylians are said to be the people 'closest to the gods'. Though most hylians do not possess innate magical abilities, hylians are best known for their proficiency in magic and artifice as well as a deep connection to the forces of destiny. They are also a people whose history is fraught with bloody conflict both within and without their mighty kingdoms and many hylian territories still bear the scars of these wars.

/
## Ball and Chain Soldier ((++Ball and Chain Soldier))

These soldiers have trained with the notorious weapon known as the ball and chain, a very large and unwieldy weapon capable of shattering armor and bone. They are often employed as prison guards, using their menacing weapons as a deterrent against prisoner uprisings.

# Kalle Demos ((+Kalle Demos))
Kalle demos are giagantic plant monsters that parasitize the Forbidden Woods, living in the deepest depths of them. It is made up of two integral parts: a vulnerable flower-like head and the multi-armed hanging bulb that not only poses a threat to prey, but shields the flower inside from damage. The bulb has two different types of tentacles: the ones that anchor the creature to the ceiling and those that act as electrified barbs.

right(
# Carnivorous Plants
Kalle demos are carnivorous but will eat plant matter just as easily as meat, as shown when one swallowed Makar of the Koroks in the Forbidden Woods.

# Keese ((+Keese))
Keese are bat-like creatures that inhabit dungeons and caves.  Keese often exist in clusters in the places where they are found. They fly around erratically, not heading towards anything in particular, and stop to rest for a short amount of time on a neighboring wall or rock face.

right(
![Keese](https://i.imgur.com/rMMOxMd.png)
)

item(
# Keese ((++Keese))
## Creature -1
-
;N,Tiny,Animal
**Perception** +6; echolocation (precise) 40 feet, low-light vision

**Skills** Acrobatics +7, Athletics +3 (+7 to Climb), Stealth +5

**Str** +1, **Dex** +3, **Con** +0, **Int** -4, **Wis** +2, **Cha** -2

**Echolocation** A keese can use its hearing as a precise sense at the listed range.
-
**AC** 15; **Fort** +1, **Ref** +8, **Will** +4

**HP** 5
-
**Speed** 5 feet, climb 5 feet, fly 20 feet

**Melee** :a: fangs +6 (agile, finesse), **Damage** 1d4 piercing

**Flying Charge** :aa: The keese spins forward batting anyone it runs into. The keese Flies in a straight line, automatically passing through creatures.  Each creature passed takes 1d4+2 bludgeoning damage (basic DC 14 Reflex save).  If a keese would end their movement in an a creature occupied square, they end up adjacent to that creature based on the direction they were traveling; if their movement takes them into a square occupied with a solid object like a wall or large statue they end their movement and take 1d4 bludgeoning damage.
)

item(
# Keese Swarm ((++Keese Swarm))

**Perception** +10; echolocation (precise) 40 feet, low-light vision

**Skills** Acrobatics +7, Athletics +3 (+7 to Climb), Stealth +7

**AC** 15; **Fort** +6, **Ref** +9, **Will** +6

**HP** 11; **Immunities** precision, swarm mind; **Resistances** bludgeoning 6, piercing 6, slashing 3; **Weaknesses** area damage 3, splash damage 3
-
**Speed** 5 feet, climb 5 feet, fly 20 feet

**Battering Swarm** :a: Each enemy in the keese swarm's space takes 1d6 bludgeoning damage (basic DC 16 Reflex save).
)

## Fire Keese ((++Fire Keese))
Fire keese are elementally charged with fire, usually roosting in areas of heavy volcanic activity.  Fire keese are more dangerous than their regular counterparts as they can set creatures on fire for a short period of time upon contact.

left(
# Fragile Flames
Fire keese that loose their flames go back to becoming normal keese.  A fire keese's flames can easily be blown away with a strong gust of wind or being submerged in water.
![Fire Keese](https://i.imgur.com/fSOZLOw.png)
)

item(
# Fire Keese
## Creature 0
-
;N,Tiny,Animal,Fire
**Perception** +6; echolocation (precise) 40 feet, low-light vision

**Skills** Acrobatics +7, Athletics +4 (+8 to Climb), Stealth +5

**Str** +1, **Dex** +3, **Con** +0, **Int** -4, **Wis** +2, **Cha** -2

**Echolocation** A keese can use its hearing as a precise sense at the listed range.
-
**AC** 16; **Fort** +2, **Ref** +9, **Will** +5

**HP** 10; **Immunities** fire

**Fiery Aura** (aura, fire) 5 feet, 1d4 fire, DC 13 basic Reflex
-
**Speed** 5 feet, climb 5 feet, fly 20 feet

**Melee** :a: fangs +6 (agile, finesse), **Damage** 1d4 piercing plus 2 fire

**Flying Charge** :aa: The keese spins forward batting anyone it runs into. The keese Flies in a straight line, automatically passing through creatures.  Each creature passed takes 1d4+2 bludgeoning damage, 1d4 fire damage, and 1 persistent fire damage (basic DC 15 Reflex save).  If a keese would end their movement in an a creature occupied square, they end up adjacent to that creature based on the direction they were traveling; if their movement takes them into a square occupied with a solid object like a wall or large statue they end their movement and take 1d4 bludgeoning damage.
)
=
## Ice Keese ((++Ice Keese))
Ice keese are elementally charged with ice, often found in cold biomes and frozen caves.  Ice keese are capable of freezing creatures that get near their icy aura.

right(
![Ice Keese](https://i.imgur.com/eYMQBj7.png)
)

item(
# Ice Keese
## Creature 1
-
;N,Tiny,Animal,Cold
**Perception** +7; echolocation (precise) 40 feet, low-light vision

**Skills** Acrobatics +7, Athletics +4 (+8 to Climb), Stealth +5

**Str** +1, **Dex** +3, **Con** +0, **Int** -4, **Wis** +2, **Cha** -2

**Echolocation** A keese can use its hearing as a precise sense at the listed range.
-
**AC** 16; **Fort** +3, **Ref** +10, **Will** +6

**HP** 12; **Immunities** cold

**Icy Aura** (aura, cold) 5 feet, 1d6 cold, DC 14 basic Fortitude
-
**Speed** 5 feet, climb 5 feet, fly 20 feet

**Melee** :a: fangs +7 (agile, finesse), **Damage** 1d6 piercing plus 2 cold

**Freezing Charge** :aa: (cold, incapacitation) The keese spins forward batting anyone it runs into. The keese Flies in a straight line, automatically passing through creatures.  Each creature passed takes 1d4+2 bludgeoning damage and 1d4 cold damage and must make a DC 16 Reflex saving throw.  If a keese would end their movement in an a creature occupied square, they end up adjacent to that creature based on the direction they were traveling; if their movement takes them into a square occupied with a solid object like a wall or large statue they end their movement and take 1d4 bludgeoning damage.
**Critical Success** The creature is not affected.
**Success** The creature takes half damage.
**Failure** The creature takes full damage and is stunned 1.
**Critical Failure** The creature takes double damage and is stunned 3.
)
=

## Dark Keese ((++Dark Keese))
Dark keese are a skeletal, undead form of the regular keese. Like some other undead monsters, they possess the ability to Curse creatures, preventing them from being able to attack.

right(
![Dark Keese](https://i.imgur.com/PAfyyyo.png)
)

item(
# Dark Keese
## Creature 2
-
;NE,Tiny,Mindless,Undead
**Perception** +8; darkvision, echolocation (precise) 40 feet

**Skills** Acrobatics +8, Athletics +7 (+9 to Climb), Stealth +7

**Str** +1, **Dex** +4, **Con** +0, **Int** -4, **Wis** +2, **Cha** -2

**Echolocation** A keese can use its hearing as a precise sense at the listed range.
-
**AC** 16; **Fort** +3, **Ref** +10, **Will** +6

**HP** 20 (void healing); **Immunities** death effects, disease, mental, paralyze, poison, sleep

**Dark Aura** (aura, curse, occult) A dark keese exudes a 5-foot aura of dark energy.  Any creature that begins its turn in the aura or is attacked by the keese must make a DC 15 Wisdom saving throw.
**Critical Success** The creature is unaffected and is temporarily immune to the dark aura for 1 hour.
**Success** The creature is unaffected and is temporarily immune to the dark aura for 1 minute.
**Failure** The creature cannot use an action with the attack trait until the end of its next turn.
**Critical Failure** The creature cannot use an action with the attack trait for 3 rounds.
-
**Speed** 5 feet, climb 10 feet, fly 25 feet

**Melee** :a: fangs +10 (agile, finesse), **Damage** 1d6+4 piercing plus Dark Aura

# Leever ((+Leever))
Leevers are sand-dwelling sandworm-like creatures known for their burrowing capabilities, found mostly in areas with sand such as deserts and beaches. These cone-shaped creatures burrow out of the ground, or remain at a semi-burrow, upon detecting movement and begin pursuing threats, generally at a fast-moving pace.  They are almost always found in groups, with many of them targeting and honing in on potential prey at once.

left(
![Leever](https://i.imgur.com/GbWUd0U.png)
)

item(
# Leever
## Creature -1
-
;N,Small,Animal
**Perception** +7; tremorsense (imprecise) 30 feet

**Skills** Stealth +5

**Str** +2, **Dex** +3, **Con** +2, **Int** -4, **Wis** +0, **Cha** -2
-
**AC** 14; **Fort** +5, **Ref** +7, **Will** +2

**HP** 7
-
**Speed** 30 feet, burrow 30 feet

**Melee** :a: jaws +7 (agile), **Damage** 1d4 piercing

**Pack Attack** The leever's Strikes deal 1d4 extra damage to creatures within reach of at least two of the leever's allies.

**Sudden Charge** :aa: The leever Strides up to double its speed in a straight line.  If the leever ends its movement within melee reach of at least one enemy, it can make a melee Strike against that enemy, with a +1 circumstance bonus to its damage roll.
)
=
# Like Like ((+Like Like))
Resembling giant sponges, like likes can be found in almost any environment, but are most abundant underwater, near coastlines, or in dank caves. They mindlessly devour anything that moves into their huge, tubular mouthes, with the intent of dissolving whatever it might be while it's still alive. The acids in its stomach can break down seemingly any material very rapidly. Even if an adventurer escapes this monster's gut alive and slays the beast, he might lose his shield, his rupees, or even his armor to its digestive acids.

/

right(
# Rupee Likes

Some like likes have a small tendril with a rupee-shaped protrusion at the end of it.  These forms of like likes, called rupee likes, hide out of sight with only the protrusion visible, waiting for potential prey to grab it.  Only then does the rupee like strike, consuming most of the prey's rupees.

![Like Like](https://i.imgur.com/HSJFupZ.png)
)

item(
# Like Like
## Creature 5
-
;N,Large,Aberration,Amphibious,Mindless
**Perception** +9; motion sense 60 feet, no vision

**Skills** Athletics +13

**Str** +5, **Dex** -5, **Con** +5, **Int** -5, **Wis** +0, **Cha** -5

**Motion Sense** A like like can sense nearby motion through vibration and air movement.
-
**AC** 13; **Fort** +15, **Ref** +7, **Will** +7

**HP** 183; **Immunities** acid, mental, poison, precision, unconsious; **Weaknesses** fire 5

**Digestion** When the like like engulfs a creature, any acid damage is dealt to its choice of the creature's armor, shield, clothing, or weapon as well as the creature, preferring to damage shields for unknown reasons.

**Damage Transfer** While the like like is engulfing a creature, the like like only takes half damage, and the engulfed creature takes the other half.

**Malleable Body** The like like's body is extreme malleable.  It has resistance 10 to extra damage from critical hits.
-
**Speed** 15 feet

**Melee** :a: slam +12 (reach 10 feet), **Damage** 2d8+7 bludgeoning plus 2d6 acid

**Engulf** :aa: DC 20, 2d8 acid, Escape DC 20, Rupture 15
)

# Lizal ((+Lizal))
Lizal are a broad and varied race of reptilian humanoids, all of whom are notorious for their cruel barbarism and esoteric ways. Although they are practically as intelligent as hylians, they are callously heartless, and come off as alien and uncanny to outsiders. Lizal consider all races other than their own—and occasionally moblins—to be either their natural enemies, or resources to be exploited. 

## Lizalfos ((++Lizalfos))
The standard lizalfos, sometimes called a geru, is seven feet tall with sleek, gecko-like scales and a bizarrely long neck; the glare emanating down upon you from a lizalfos' unfeeling eyes is more than enough to send a shiver down your spine. They are also the most culturally capable and organized, as they have been known to create large fortifications in what domains they call their own.

/

left(
# Lizalfos Pairs
Lizalfos pair up with each other when fighting, allowing them to flank a solitary target in combat.

![Lizalfos](https://i.imgur.com/D9bTqcg.png)
)

item(

**Leap Attack** :aa: The lizalfos Strides up to twice its Speed, during which it attempts a High Jump or a Long Jump.  At any point during its movement, the lizalfos can make a melee Strike against an enemy in its reach.  The lizalfos then can't use Leap Attack for 1 round.

**Paired Tactics** The lizalfos' Strikes deal 1d6 extra damage to creatures within the reach of exactly one of the lizalfos' allies.
)
=
## Aeralfos ((++Aeralfos))
The aeralfos is shorter, thinner, and more fragile than most lizalfos—standing just over 5 feet tall. Its lightweight body combined with powerful, bat-like wings give it terrific flying ability. Its diving sword attacks are lethal, even more so when a land-bound target has no way to retaliate. 

right(
# Denizens of the Sky
The aeralfos are often found in the ancient sky ruins known as the City in the Sky, where they can fly from room to room without fear of falling to their death.

![Aeralfos](https://i.imgur.com/cauuMSs.png)
)

If the attack misses, the aeralfos deflected it with its shield.  It cannot use this ability to deflect unusually large or heavy ranged projectiles (such as boulders or ballista bolts).

=
## Dinolfos ((++Dinolfos))
Even though it stands hunched over, the reptilian dinolfos towers a good foot over most other humanoids, and has a muscular frame. Its scales are a deep green color, with accents of brown and pale yellow. Distinctly among lizalfos, an array of thorny spines run from its scalp down its back to the tip of its tail.

Like lizalfos, dinolfos generally prefer humid environments with abundant fauna on which to feed, like swamps and jungles. However, they've also been known to inhabit inhospitably hot environments—mainly the caverns of active volcanoes.

left(
# Affinity for Fire
Dinolfos prefer to live hotter environments, such as volcanoes, and have the ability to breathe blasts of fire, unlike most of their lizal brethren.

![Dinolfos](https://i.imgur.com/ckYQSxI.png)
)

## Fiery Aeralfos ((++Fiery Aeralfos))
Whether by natural means or a magical enhancement, the core of a fiery aeralfos burns with draconic fire, and its scales glow a reddish color as a result. Its torso is visibly aflame with magic fire at all times, radiating searing heat and dim light. The aeralfos is no longer harmed by heat, but it cannot extinguish its own flames even if it wants to. 

right(
# Draconic Heritage
Not much is known about how a fiery aeralfos comes to be, though they are rumored to be offspring of dragons and lizal.

Larger and more powerful than their regular cousins, dark lizalfos are capable of breathing a smoky caliginous breath, which curses a creature into being unable to attack. Dark lizalfos love to taunt their enemies while flanking and can use their gauntlets as makeshift shields.

# Lynel ((+Lynel))

These fearsome monsters have lived in Hyrule since ancient times. They possess intense intelligence, resilience, and strength, making them among the most dangerous monsters in all the land. This is compounded by the fact that they have a natural resistance to all elements. You would be wise to challenge a Lynel only if you're very well prepared.

/

left(
# Lynel Colors
A lynel can be of a variety of colors, with red being the most common.
![Red Lynel](https://i.imgur.com/bjzMp2N.png)
)

**Breath Weapon** :aa: (arcane, fire) The lynel breathes a blast of fire that explodes in a 15-foot burst within 50 feet, dealing 8d6 fire damage (DC 28 basic Reflex save). Creatures that fail the save also take 2d6 persistent fire damage. The lynel can't use Breath Weapon again for 1d4 rounds.

**Trample** :aaa: Medium or smaller, hoof, DC 28.  Creatures that take damage are knocked prone.
)

**Variant Options.** You can swap out the *lesser flaming composite longbow* for a *lesser shock composite longbow* or *lesser frost composite longbow*.  You can also swap out the *+1 striking spear* for a *+1 striking longsword* and *steel shield* (adding Shield Block as a reaction) for the Lynel Sword weapon or a *+1 striking greatclub* for the Lynel Crusher weapon.

# Magtail ((+Magtail))
Magtails are arthropods covered in a hard exoskeleton that not even the searing heat of lava can penetrate. Their exoskeleton is hard enough to deflect most attacks, with their eyes are their only weakness. When harmed, magtails curl up into a defensive position, which can be picked up and carried around.

left(
# Larval Fire Gohma?
Magtails seem to bear some resemblence to the gargantuan fire gohma, suggesting that they are the larval stage of that enormous monster, but this is merely speculation by some and not confirmed.  GMs that wish to play into this theory may add the gohma trait to the magtail.

)

A large man-eating flower with jaw-like leaves sticking out in all four directions.  It moves faster as it loses its leaves.  Even though it is a plant, manhandla are capable of spitting motes of fire and appear to be immune to fire themselves.

item(
# Manhandla ((++Manhandla))
## Creature 10
-
;Uncommon,N,Huge,Mindless,Plant
**Perception** +17; tremorsense (imprecise) 60 feet

**Skills** Athletics +23, Stealth +21 (+24 in undergrowth)

**Str** +7, **Dex** +5, **Con** +5, **Int** -5, **Wis** +3, **Cha** -2
-
**AC** 29, all-around vision; **Fort** +21, **Ref** +17, **Will** +15

**HP** 180 (45 HP per leaf); **Immunities** fire, mental; **Resistances** acid 10

**Multiple Leaves** (vulnerability) The manhandla has four jaw-like leaves, each of which have 45 Hit Points comprising the total Hit Points of the manhandla, but are tracked separately.  A specific leaf can be targeted with a -2 circumstance penalty.  An attack that does not target a specific leaf simply damages a leaf at random.  Each leaf that is destroyed adds a cumulative +5-foot status bonus to the manhandla's Speed.

**Reactive Strike** :r: Leaf only.
-
**Speed** 25 feet

**Melee** :a: leaf +23 (reach 15 feet), **Damage** 2d8+7 piercing plus 2d6 acid

**Melee** :a: slam +23, **Damage** 2d12+9 bludgeoning 

**Ranged** :a: firebolt +21 (fire, primal, range 60 feet), **Damage** 6d6 fire

**Focused Assault** :aa:  The manhandla attacks a single target with all four of its leaves.  The manhandla makes one leaf Strike.  On a success, the manhandla deals the damage from one leaf Strike plus an additional 1d8 damage for every leaf beyond the first.  On a failure, the manhandla deals the damage from one leaf Strike.  It deals no damage on a critical failure.  This counts toward the manhandla’s multiple attack penalty as a number of attacks equal to the number of leaves the manhandla has.

**Hungry Flurry** :aa: The manhandla makes four leaf Strikes at a –2 penalty, each against a different target. These attacks count toward the manhandla’s multiple attack penalty, but the multiple attack penalty doesn’t increase until after it makes all its attacks.

**Spinning Dash** :aa: The manhandla dashes around at high speeds.  It Strides twice and then makes a slam Strike.
)

The medusa head can deactivate or activate this aura by using a single action, which has the concentrate trait.

After attempting its save, the creature is then temporarily immune until the start of the medusa head's next turn.
