If the creature was already slowed by petrifying gaze before attempting the save, a failed save causes it to be petrified for 1 round (or permanently on a critical failure).  If the medusa head critically succeeds on its attack roll, use the outcome for one degree of success worse than the result of the save.  After attempting its save, the creature is then temporarily immune until the start of the medusa head's next turn.

# Molduga ((+Molduga))
This massive monster swims beneath the desert's sand. The molduga spends most of its time submerged, but if it senses sound, it will breach the surface to feast on whatever it can grab. Running around carelessly can be dangerous if you suspect there may be one in the area.

/

left(
# Deep Desert Dwellers
Molduga are rarely found outside the deep desert, but they have been known to dig close to Gerudo settlements, prompting the desert people to send hunters after them.

# Valuable Guts
The guts of a slain molduga are a valuable ingredient in making elixirs.  Oftentimes, groups of hunters venture forth into the deep desert in search of these rare and valuable materials.
)

# Molduking ((++Molduking))
An exceptionally old and powerful molduga, the molduking is a survivor of many attempts to hunt it.  The molduking has absorbed iron into its skin to bolster its defensive capabilities far beyond its molduga counterparts, though at the cost of granting it a minor vulnerability to electricity.

/

left(
# Survivor of Many Battles

Some molduking still retain fragments of broken blades and spears in its tough hide, remnants of countless failed attempts to fell the beast.  If you wish to portray a survivor of many battles, you can add the following defensive ability to a molduking's statblock after applying the Elite adjustment:

**Broken Arsenal** Fragments of broken blades and spears, the remnants of countless failed attempts to fell the beast, remain lodged in the molduking's flesh.  When an adjacent creature hits the molduking with a melee attack or otherwise touches it, that creature takes 8 piercing damage.
)

# Morpha ((+Morpha))

A morpha appears as a small violet or red orb the size of a hylian's head, surrounded with a slimy, crackling, and semitransparent membrane. One is never found out of a body of water. A morpha is not merely aquatic, but is able to magically manipulate the water around it. It does so to swim at incredibly high speeds, and can even form limbs out of water around itself to grab prey much larger than its body.

Encounters with a morpha are quite rare, but more often than not it is the result of water seeming to come alive and reach out of a lake, pond, or coastline to drag an individual to their death. Underwater, a morpha can slowly dissolve and digest virtually any corpse with the acidic membrane that immediately surrounds its body.

/

left(
![Morpha](https://i.imgur.com/WHWXEoE.png)
)

item(
# Morpha
## Creature 8
-
;Rare,N,Small,Mindless,Ooze,Water
**Perception** +15; motion sense 120 feet, no vision

**Skills** Athletics +18

**Str** +7, **Dex** -4, **Con** +7, **Int** -5, **Wis** +0, **Cha** -5

**Motion Sense** A morpha can sense nearby creatures through vibration and air or water movement.
-
**AC** 18; **Fort** +16, **Ref** +11, **Will** +12

**HP** 194; **Immunities** cold, critical hits, mental, piercing, precision, slashing, unconscious, visual; **Resistances** acid 10; **Weaknesses** aquatic dependence, electricity 10

**Aquatic Dependence** (vulnerability) While the morpha's core is not submerged in water, it cannot cannot manifest water pseudopods and loses its immunity to piercing and slashing damage as well as critical hits.  The morpha is stunned 2 whenever it is brought out of water.
-
**Speed** 15 feet, swim 40 feet

**Melee** :a: pseudopod +18 (reach 10 feet), **Damage** 2d8+9 bludgeoning plus 2d6 acid and Grab

**Constrict** :a: 1d8+9 bludgeoning plus 1d6 acid, DC 27

**Manifest Water Pseudopod** :a: (water) The morpha manifests a water pseudopod from a body of water within 120 feet of the morpha's core.  It can use this manifested pseudopod to make a Strike with a pseudopod at any target within range.  The morpha can have up to five pseudopods manifested at any one time.  Each manifested pseudopod lasts until the morpha Dismisses it as a free action.

**Pseudopod Barrage** :aaa: The morpha makes a single pseudopod Strike with its primary pseudopod and each additional pseudopod it has manifested.  It does not increase its multiple attack penalty until after all attacks have been made.
)
=
# Morpheel ((+Morpheel))
A morpheel is a large, eel-like, aquatic monster corrupted by Twili magic.  It has a slender body that is covered in red and green scales.  Its body is segmented into vertebrae-like sections that are largest near the head and taper towards the tail.  Each of these sections have a set of longer fins that come out of its back and underbelly.  The tail has a large fan-like fin.  Two other similar fins are located on opposite sides of the head.  On its head, a morpheel has a mouth-like opening with twelve sharp, white barbs.  This protects a smaller, sphincter-like mouth that has finer barbs on its surface.  This inner mouth can produce bomb fish.  Morpheel has eight long, iridescent tentacles around its head.  A ring-like light occasionally flows through them, but the tentacles are not electrified.   The morpheel has a single eyeball that is free to move throughout each tentacle.  This eyeball can rest in a socket on the morpheel's back near its head, too.

right(
![Morpheel](https://i.imgur.com/tpQuLI9.png)
)

**HP** 200; **Resistances** physical 10

**Vulnerable Eye** (vulnerability) The morpheel's eye is particularly vulnerable, being able to be pulled out of the morpheel's body to be struck before it bounces back into the body.  Once the eye has been identified as a weak spot, a creature may attempt a DC 30 Athletics check to pull the eye out of morpheel's body.  When exposed in this manner, the morpheel's eye has weakness 10 to damage and the morpheel's resistance does not apply to the eye.  The morpheel's eye will bounce back into the morpheel's body at the start of the morpheel's next turn.

The bomb fish explode near creatures in the area, dealing 6d6 sonic damage plus 5d6 fire damage (DC 29 basic Fortitude).  If no creatures are in the area covered by the cone, the bomb fish linger in the cone's area ready to explode until the start of the morpheel's next turn when they swim away.  The morpheel can't use Spit Bomb Fish again for 1d6 rounds.

# Mothula ((+Mothula))
Mothula are large moth-like creatures that can fly around at high speeds using a jet of flame they produce in their bodies.  Young mothula are called morths, which mothula are capable of laying rapidly to stick to either threats or prey to slow them down, either as a defense mechanism or a way to make potential prey easier to capture.

right(

Some mothula have their wings already clipped.  These wingless mothula tend to be more aggressive to make up for lack of flight for protection.

**Rocket Charge** :aa:  The mothula Flies twice using its fly Speed. If it ends its movement within melee reach of one creature, it can make a mandibles Strike against that creature, except the damage is 3d8+10 and the attack gains Knockdown.

The mothula can't use Spray Morth again for 1d4 rounds.  Adjacent allies of a creature with morths attached to them can spend an action to remove the morths from the creature, which ends the slowed condition and penalty to Speed immediately.
**Critical Success** The creature is unaffected.
**Success** The creature takes no damage, but is slowed 1 until the end of its next turn.
**Failure** The creature takes 5d6 piercing damage and is slowed 2 until the end of its next turn.
**Critical Failure** As failure, but the damage is doubled and the creature is slowed 2 and has a -10-foot penalty to its Speeds for 1 minute.

# Octorok ((+Octorok))
Octoroks are highly adaptable omnivorous creatures. As their name implies, octoroks bear similarities to octopi, and famously spit rocks as their primary form of attack. They can be almost any color, but are most often violet, red, or blue. An octorok has between four and eight tentacle-like legs which are surprisingly functional both on land and in water, enabling octoroks to be truly amphibious.

/

## Big Octo ((++Big Octo))

Rarely, a normal octorok is able to grow to this immense size, and produces a natural snail-like shell it uses as armor. Unlike normal octoroks, a big octo does not often hunt by spitting rocks, but instead uses the sheer size and power of its body to tackle and crush prey. It is known to swallow fish, birds, and even people whole, digesting them while they yet live.

# Phantom Rider ((+Phantom Rider))
Phantom riders appear as humanoid figures wearing heavy armor with horned helmets. They wield large lances or longswords. A phantom rider can be summoned into existence through powerful dark magic, and will aid the creature that brought them forward with unyielding allegiance. They typically appear in groups of three, with a single leader and two flanking allies.

# Poe ((+Poe))
Poes are spirits of the dead that became monsters because of an unresolved attachment to the mortal world.  They always carry a lantern that acts as a container for the poe's soul, and can turn invisible at will, though the lantern will remain visible.

/
## Lantern Poe ((++Lantern Poe))
Lantern poes are cloaked spirits, taking on the appearance of hooded wraiths with glowing eyes, that freely roam graveyards and other haunted locales about Hyrule and other lands.

left(
# Soul Lantern
Poes carry a lantern with them that serves as the container for that specific poe soul, which is also the only part of them that will not turn invisible.

**Occult Innate Spells** DC 36; **3rd** *haste*, **1st** *fear* (x3), **Constant (2nd)** *see invisiblity*

**Infuse Weapon** Any scythe gains the agile trait, can’t be disarmed, and becomes a *+2 greater striking keen* scythe while the grim repoe wields it.

**Spin Attack** :aa: (flourish) The grim repoe Strides two times, spinning its scythe as it does so.  The grim repoe makes a melee Strike against each creature in range as it Strides.  Each attack counts towards the grim repoe's multiple attack penalty, but penalty doesn't increase until after it has made all attacks.

**Whiff Out Light** :aa: (darkness) The grim repoe blows out all light sources within 120 feet, creating a 120-foot emanation of darkness.  Treat this darkness as if it was cast from a 4th-level *darkness* spell.

# Redead ((+Redead))

## Redead  ((++Redead))
A vaguely humanoid-shaped monstrosity of dull color, a redead is renowned for instilling such fear that its victim completely loses the capability to move. Once a victim is immobilized by terror, the redead lurches towards it with eerily slow movement. The monster's four leathery limbs all wrap around its victim at once—further immobilizing the poor creature—and the redead's blunt teeth begin to tear and devour the paralyzed victim while it still lives. The few who have survived this experience are known to retain mind-rattling nightmares of it for the rest of their days.

/

right(
# The Moaning Dead
Redead appear in small groups or sometimes alone in dead or ruinous places, such as tombs or dungeons, and make their presence known with periodic, low-pitched moans.

)

**Feast** :aa: (manipulate) If the redead is adjacent to a helpless or unconscious creature, a creature it has Grabbed, or a deceased creature that died in the past hour, the redead can feast upon its flesh to heal itself. This restores an amount of Hit Points equal to the redead's level. If the creature is alive, the redead deals damage equal to its fist damage.

**Paralyzing Shriek** :aa: (auditory, emotion, fear, incapacitation, mental) The redead unleashes a horrifying shriek.  Each creature within a 60-foot burst must attempt a DC 20 Will save.  Regardless of the outcome of their saving throw, affected creatures are then immune to Paralyzing Shriek for 1 hour.  The redead can't use Paralyzing Shriek again for 1d4 rounds.
**Critical Success** The creature is unaffected.
**Success** The creature is frightened 2.
**Failure** The creature is frightened 2 and paralyzed for 1 round.
**Critical Failure** The creature is frightened 3 and paralyzed for 1d4 rounds.

## Redead Knight ((++Redead Knight))
A particularly powerful redead, known for their stature and wielding colossal weapons. It is of greater physical size and strength than their lessers, but of the same horrifying visage and demeanor. A knight seems to usually be the result of a redead that animates from the dead of either gerudo warriors or darknuts, as the knights are most abundant where these races have previously thrived.

# Sheikah ((+Sheikah))
The Sheikah are a humanoid race, bearing great resemblance to Hylians in both appearance and magical capacity.  They are a mysterious and secretive tribe with pointed ears, red eyes, and shadowy magic abilities.  They have often served as the guardians of the Royal Family.

### Yiga Clan ((++Yiga Clan))
The Yiga clan are a clan of Sheikah that have devoted themselves to serving the forces of darkness, particularly Ganon, after being shunned by the very kingdom they once protected, and seek to destroy those who would stand against him.  They formed after the Sheikah were exiled in fear of the advanced technology they had developed.
=

# Skulltula ((+Skulltula))

A typical skulltula is a spider-like, eight-legged monstrosity that is the size of an adult hylian. Its hardened, armor-like carapace bears a striking resemblance to a large humanoid skull, hence the origin of the creature's name. Although these creatures can lay webbing traps like more mundane spiders, more often than not they actively hunt their prey. They are unusually skilled at melee combat, and some have even been known to block sword strikes.

Skulltulas usually dwell in areas of darkness, most commonly including caverns and forest depths. Small, young skulltulas are most often referred to as walltulas, and have fewer capabilities compared to their elders. If an area has even one skulltula or walltulla, there are usually a dozen or more hiding in the darkness nearby.

left(
![Skulltula](https://i.imgur.com/Uzuvd6K.jpg)
)

# Skytail ((+Skytail))
Skytails are giant, winged monsters that live inside large thunderclouds such as the Thunderhead. They fly in winding, twirling motions, usually in small groups. When they spot prey flying in their domain, they will congregate on the prey's location and charge at them, aiming to bite them with their large pincers. Their movements are meandering and unpredictable, making them difficult to avoid and damage.

# Snapper ((+Snapper))

A snapper appears as a monstrous tortoise with a pointed beak like that of a snapping turtle, hence its name. Its gigantic, bulbous shell is nearly as tall and wide as an adult man, and is almost impossible to penetrate with most weaponry. A snapper is capable of retreating into its shell and using it to charge at a target.

# Snurgle ((+Snurgle))
Snurgles resemble small, flying elephants. They are often found while riding the Spirit Train across New Hyrule, but can be found in plains or other wide-open areas. Snurgles fly around for a few seconds before trumpeting and swooping in for an attack. They can be temporarily stunned by making a loud noise, such as blowing a train's whistle, or by firing a cannon to shoot them out of the sky.  If there is cargo being transported, snurgles will attempt to steal it instead of attacking.

# Stagnox ((+Stagnox))
Stagnox are large stag beetles that roam dense forests.  They are heavily armored up front and protect their less armored backsides by producing noxious fumes that drive away creatures that get near it.

right(
# Interactive Blastworms
Perceptive adventurers will note that the blastworms a stagnox lays do not explode immediately.  A creature may spend two actions: an Interact action to pick up the blastworm, and an action with the attack trait to throw the blastworm up to 30 feet away.

![Stagnox](https://i.imgur.com/FYWHVHT.png)

**Noxious Fumes** (aura, inhaled, poison) 5 feet, 2d8 poison, DC 20 basic Fortitude

**Vulnerable Backside**  (vulnerability) The stagnox's backside is not as well protected as its front, though it is covered in noxious fumes.  A creature may use a directed air effect, such as *gust of wind*, to blow the fumes away, which disables the stagnox's Noxious Fumes aura until the end of the stagnox's next turn.  While its Noxious Fumes is disabled, a creature may target the stagnox's backside.  The stagnox has weakness 5 to damage dealt to its backside.

These blastworms detonate at the end of the stagnox's next turn, dealing 3d6 fire damage to all creatures within 5 feet of at least one blastworm (DC 22 basic Reflex save).  The stagnox can't use Blastworm Blitz again for 1d4+1 rounds.

**Stagnox Charge** :aa: The stagnox Strides or Flies twice, then makes a horn Strike. As long as the stagnox moved at least 20 feet, the Strike's damage increases to 3d10+6.  A Medium or smaller creature struck by this attack must succeed at a DC 22 Reflex save or be automatically Shoved back 5 feet and knocked prone by the force of the blow.

**Trample** :aaa: Large or smaller, foot, DC 19

# Stal ((+Stal))

Made from bones held together by foul necromancy, stal creatures are among the most common types of undead.  The word "stal" is Hylian for skeleton.  They are often found haunting old dungeons and forgotten cemetaries.

## Stal Abilities

Some stal creatures have one or more of these abilities.  If you give a stal creature more than one, you might want to increase its level and adjust its statistics, or apply the Sunlight Vulnerability ability to weaken them in sunlight to compensate for the additional power of its other abilities.
item(
**Blaze** The stal is wreathed in fire, which doesn't consume its bones or gear.  The stal gains immunity to fire and weakness 5 to cold, loses its resistance to cold, and its Strikes deal additional persistant fire damage equal to half the stal's level (minimum 1 damage).

**Bloody** The stal is covered in dripping blood and gains fast healing equal to its level.

**Bone Missile** :aa: The stal yanks a rib from its ribcage to use as an arrow or javelin.  The stal loses HP equal to its level (minimum 1), then makes a ranged Strike.  This uses the attack bonus of whichever of the stal's other Strikes has the highest attack bonus and deals piercing damage equal to the Strike's damage plus the skeleton's level (minimum 1).

**Bone Powder** When the stal takes physical damage from a critical hit, one of its bones is pulverized into a fine powder.  All creatures in a 5-foot emanation that breathe take 1d6 persistent poison damage (plus an additional 1d6 for every 6 levels the stal has).

**Collapse** :r: **Trigger** The stal is critically hit. **Effect** The stal collapses into a pile of bones and the attack deals only normal damage.  The stal can then reform in a standing position as an action, but until it does, it is immobilized and flat-footed.

**Explosive Death** When the stal is destroyed, its bones shatter and explode as the necromantic energy holding it together is released.  Adjacent creatures take 1d6 slashing damage per 2 levels (minimum 1d6) with a basic Reflex save.

**Screaming Skull** :aa: (auditory, emotion, fear, mental) The stal removes its skull and throws it, making a jaws attack with a range of 20 feet.  It then attempts to Demoralize each foe within 10 feet of the target.  The head bounces, rolls, or even flies back, returning to the stal at the start of its next turn.  The stal is blind until then.

**Sunlight Vulnerability** (vulnerability) If exposed to direct sunlight, the stal becomes slowed 1. The slowed value increases by 1 each time the stal ends its turn in sunlight. If the stal loses all its actions this way, it is destroyed.
)
=

## Stalhound ((++Stalhound))
A stalhound is the resurrected bones of a dog. They have been known to be used by stalblin and stalfos as pack hunters, much like a normal hunter and his dog. They otherwise roam the countryside after dark, in search of prey.

## Stalkoblin ((++Stalkoblin))
The stalkoblin is the resurrected skeleton of a bokoblin, usually raised by dark magic.  They are individually very weak, but the numerous bokoblins that have been killed by adventurers throughout Hyrule makes them a very common sight after dark away from heavily populated areas.

left(

## Stalfos ((++Stalfos))
Taking the form of a humanoid animated skeleton, the exact construction and nature of a stalfos varies slightly with the race to which its body once belonged. In virtually all cases, a stalfos wields above-average power and fortitude thanks to the necromantic magic that empowers its eternal body.

Stalfos are seen as the most common form of humanoid stal creatures. They typically wield common or makeshift weapons, and can jump to uncanny heights thanks to the lightweight nature of their bodies. An average stalfos retain more mobility than the relatively sluggish stalchild, but lacks the inherent martial prowess of a stalfos knight or the vile magic of a dark stalfos.

/

right(
# Agile Jumpers

Stalfos are eeriely agile for skeletal creatures.  They often jump long distances to either make an attack or to dodge out of an incoming attack.

![Stalfos](https://i.imgur.com/We9kMSF.png)
)

## Staldra ((++Staldra))

left(
![Staldra](https://i.imgur.com/0yOoR5c.png)
)

One of the most fearsome of stal creatures, the staldra is the skeleton of an ancient multiheaded snake said to exist before the dawn of time. Three bone-plated heads and a thirst to cause pain keep it writhing even beyond death.
/
item (
# Staldra
## Creature 8
-
;Uncommon,NE,Huge,Mindless,Stal,Undead
**Perception** +19; darkvision

**Skills** Athletics +19, Stealth +14

**Str** +6, **Dex** +4, **Con** +4, **Int** -4, **Wis** +2, **Cha** -2
-
**AC** 26 all-around vision; **Fort** +19, **Ref** +16, **Will** +13

**HP** 130 ((body) void healing, staldra regeneration) **Immunities** bleed, death effects, disease, mental, paralyze, poison, unconscious; **Resistances** cold 10, electricity 10, fire 10, piercing 10, slashing 10

**HP** 25 ((head) void healing, head regrowth); **Immunities** area damage, bleed, death effects, disease, mental, paralyze, poison, unconscious; **Resistances** cold 5, electricity 5, fire 5, piercing 5

**Head Regrowth** A staldra ordinarily has three heads. A creature can attempt to sever one of the staldra's heads by specifically targeting it and dealing damage equal to the head’s Hit Points. A head that is not completely severed returns to full Hit Points at the end of any creature’s turn.
A staldra can regrow a severed head using Staldra Regeneration. A creature can prevent this regrowth by dealing vitalic damage to the stump, cauterizing it. Single-target vitalic effects need to be targeted at a specific stump, but effects that deal splash damage or affect areas covering the hydra’s whole space cauterize all stumps if they deal vitalic damage. If the attack that severs a head deals any vitalic damage, the stump is cauterized instantly. If all three heads are cauterized, the staldra dies.

**Multiple Opportunities** A staldra gains an extra reaction per round for each of its heads beyond the first, which it can use only to make Reactive Strikes. It can’t use more than 1 reaction on the same triggering action, even if a creature leaves several squares within its reach, and the staldra must use a different head for each Reactive Strike it makes. Whenever one of the staldra's heads is severed, the staldra loses 1 of its extra reactions per round.

**Reactive Strike** :r:

**Staldra Regeneration** The staldra has regeneration equal to 5 x the number of heads it has. If a staldra's body is missing any heads and the remaining stumps have not been cauterized, the staldra attempts a DC 23 Fortitude save after it regains Hit Points from regeneration.  On a success, it regrows all heads that have been severed.  The staldra's regeneration only fully deactivates if all its heads are severed at once and all stumps are cauterized, at which point it dies.
-
**Speed** 25 feet, swim 25 feet

**Melee** :a: jaws +19 (reach 10 feet), **Damage** 2d8+8 piercing
)
=
item(
**Focused Assault** :aa: The staldra attacks a single target with its heads, overwhelming its foe with multiple attacks and leaving almost nowhere to dodge. The staldra Strikes with its jaws. On a successful attack, the staldra deals damage from its jaws Strike to the target, plus an additional 1d8 damage for every head it has beyond the first. Even on a failed attack, the staldra deals the damage from one jaws Strike to the target creature, though it still misses completely on a critical failure. This counts toward the staldra’s multiple attack penalty as a number of attacks equal to the number of heads the staldra has.

**Storm of Jaws** :aa: The staldra makes a number of Strikes up to its number of heads, each against a different target.  These attacks count towards the staldra's multiple attack penalty, but the multiple attack penalty doesn't increase until after the staldra makes all its attacks.
)

## Stalnox ((++Stalnox))
The mere remains of what was once a giant monster known as a hinox.  These skeletal beasts appear at nighttime.  Much like their living counterparts, the stalnox will tear entire trees from the ground to use as weapons.  Furthermore, even if it appears defeated at first, it will keep coming back for more as long as its eye is left intact.

# Taros ((+Taros))

Wild and ferocious bull-like humanoids, taros are a race of fiendish warriors native to the Dark World, a dark reflection of the Light World. As the bandits they so infamously are, taros crave nothing above violence and material wealth. They operate in loose, bestial bands that dwell in fields and mountains. These bandit tribes are infamous for raiding caravans and sacking villages alike. When paid well, however, they can be surprisingly loyal mercenaries.

/
left(
# Dark World Native
Taros are native to the warped realm that is the Dark World, a world that has succumbed to the wish of the Gerudo thief, Ganondorf.  They are analogous to the moblins found in the Light World, but their bullish features betray their fiendish heritage.

![Taros](https://i.imgur.com/nIRwRBN.png)

# Tektite ((+Tektite))

Four-limbed, one-eyed carnivorous insects, tektites are well-known to jump great distances as their primary form of movement. They usually hunt in groups of three to eight. These tektite packs have an odd tactic: they leap great distances, then bodyslam their hard underbellies and legs into the prey with the intention of breaking bones and preventing escape. Once a foe is sufficiently unable to resist, they slowly devour the prey in nibbling bites—often while it is still alive. Tektites hunt indiscriminately, slamming into everything from small birds to traveling merchants, but rarely approach foes several times their size.

/
right(
# Water Striders
Tektites are light enough to be able to stride upon the surface of water without sinking.
![Tektite](https://i.imgur.com/sB8GT50.png)
)

# Twili ((+Twili))
The twili are a race of shadow beings who inhabit the Twilight Realm.  Although usually a peaceful tribe, the Twili have been known to be transformed into hideous creatures known as shadow beasts by powerful dark magic to invade Hyrule or other regions of the Light World.

The twili are descendants of a tribe of hylian sorcerers from Hyrule, who are referred to as Interlopers.  Eons ago, the Interlopers were condemned to the Twilight Realm by the Golden Goddesses of Hyrule as punishment for their misgoverned attempt to use magic to claim the Triforce.  Their old magic became known as the Fused Shadow, an instrument of dark power.  However, during their failed attempt to conquer the Sacred Realm, their Fused Shadow was split into four pieces and scattered throughout the Twilight Realm and Hyrule.  The tribe lived and evolved in the Twilight Realm for centuries in isolation, mere shadows of what they once were, as over time they became accustomed to their surroundings and came to accept their fate.  While some learned to love the beautiful peace that could only be found in Twilight, others felt that they were being oppressed by the people of the Light World.  The twili lost their most powerful abilities but they still possess some magical power and teleportation is possible for the strongest twili.

The twili have glowing markings on their skin, which is black and pale bluish-gray in color.  This complexion may be due to lack of full light as the twili transformed after they were ejected from the World of Light. They also have oval eyes that are normally red, yellow, or orange.  They are usually quite thin and much taller than hylians.
=
## Shadow Emissary ((++Shadow Emissary))
Shadow emissaries are bestial forms of twili warped by dark magic, either a predecessor of the magic used to produce the more widely known shadow beasts or intentionally designed to produce more bestial servants.  They are usually sent early in twili invasions to clear out regions before the main twili force arrives.  Shadow emissaries are incredibly vicious and will not let up once their target is in their grasp, gnawing with powerful jaws.

# Wallmaster ((+Wallmaster))

A wallmaster appears as a gigantic and disembodied humanoid hand of a jet black and slightly violet color, usually with sharpened nails. It crawls along walls and ceilings of vile temples, corrupted ruins, or other structures filled with dark magic. Not needing to eat or even breathe, one these magically created creatures exists solely to protect its habitat from invaders. If any foreign entity enters the structure it guards, the wallmaster falls upon it, clutching it tightly in its grip. In a blur of black smoke, the clutched victim is knocked unconscious and returned to the entrance of whatever structure the wallmaster is protecting.

A wallmaster is able to maneuver overground by crawling on its five huge fingers. More often than not, however, a wallmaster will magically fly back up to the spot from which it pounced, waiting eternally for the next invader.

Wallmasters are related to floormasters, and usually bear an almost identical appearance. Unlike a floormaster, a wallmaster sticks to ceilings and walls, and almost always attacks by dropping on its victims and teleporting them away. A wallmaster lacks the more robust combat abilities of a floormaster, and most floormasters lack the ability to teleport victims

/

left(
# Rarely Deadly
Wallmasters rarely kill their victims, instead preferring to just drag them back to the entrance of whatever region they are found in.

![Wallmaster](https://i.imgur.com/qX5fIwb.png)
)

# Wizzrobe ((+Wizzrobe))

These spell-casting monsters can be found all over Hyrule. They use their fire rods to create fireballs or to summon fiery monsters and have been known to rapidly increase the temperature in the area until it is scorching hot. The temperature will normalize once the wizzrobe is defeated.

# Zora ((+Zora))
The Zora are an aquatic folk who possess fish and amphibian like traits, including fins, webbed feet and gills, which allow them to swim and thrive underwater. Zora can come in many shapes and sizes, but are most commonly depicted as humanoids with long tail fins on their heads and finned appendages on their arms and legs.  Zora are normally found in or near large bodies of water, but very rarely stray far away from them.

/

**Melee** :a: bladed fin +17 (finesse, unarmed), **Damage** 2d6+10 slashing

**Melee** :a: foot +16 (agile, nonlethal, unarmed), **Damage** 2d6+6 bludgeoning

**Ranged** :a: bladed fin +17 (thrown 15 feet, unarmed), **Damage** 2d6+10 slashing

**Flurry of Blows** :a: (flourish) The zora makes two unarmed Strikes.  If both hit the same creature, combine their damage for the purpose of resistances and weaknesses.

**Reflective Ripple Stance** :a: (stance, water) The zora enters a stance of fluid grace as small amounts of water flow with their movements and attacks.  The zora's bladed fin unarmed attack gains the water trait while in this stance.  The zora gains a +1 circumstance bonus to Athletics checks to Disarm, Swim, or Trip, and gains a +2 circumstance bonus to their Reflex DC to avoid being Disarmed and Tripped.

**Wave Spiral** :aa:  (water) **Frequency** once per minute; **Requirement** The zora is in Reflective Ripple Stance; **Effect** The zora dips and spins, unleashing a wide whirlpool of water.  They make an Athletics check to Trip each creature standing on the ground in a 10-foot emanation.  These attacks all count toward the zora's multiple attack penalty, but the penalty doesn't increase until after the zora makes all the attacks.
)

# Beamos ((+Beamos))
## Hazard 3
-
;Complex, Electricity, Magical
**Complexity** Complex

**Stealth** DC 15 (untrained)

**Description** A spherical eye made of stone or metal rests atop an 8-foot tall pillar, opening only when a creature comes within 30 feet.
-
**Disable** Thievery, DC 20 (expert) to disable the beamos by removing the eye, or triggering an explosion using a bomb to destroy the pillar.

**AC** 19; **Fort** +8, **Ref** +5

**Beamos Hardness** 15, **Beamos HP** 60 (BT 30); **Immunities** critical hits, object immunities, precision damage

**Eye Beam** :r: **Trigger** A creature walks within 30 feet of the beamos.  **Effect**  The beamos activates and fires a beam of energy at the triggering creature, then rolls initiative.
-
**Beam** :a: (arcane, electricity) The beamos fires a beam of energy in a 30-foot line that deals 2d12 electricity damage (DC 18 basic Reflex save).

**HP** 20 (BT 10); **Immunities** mental, poison; **Weaknesses** slashing 5

**Melee** :a: jaws +8 (reach 10 feet), **Damage** 1d6+2 piercing plus Baba Poison

**Baba Poison** (poison); **Saving Throw** DC 13 Fortitude; **Maximum Duration** 3 rounds; **Stage 1** sickened 1 (1 round), **Stage 2** sickened 2 (1 round)

# Spinning Ice Scythe ((+Spinning Ice Scythe))
## Hazard 8
-
;Cold,Mechanical,Simple,Water
**Complexity** Simple

**Stealth** +16 (expert) 

**Description** A pair of large blades of ice attached to a pillar of ice spin in place, covering a large area.
-
**Disable** Thievery, DC 28 (expert) to disconnect the spinning mechanism

**AC** 26, **Fort** +20, **Ref** +12

**Pillar Hardness** 15, **Pillar HP** 72 (BT 36); **Immunities** critical hits, object immunities, precision damage; **Weaknesses** fire 10
-
**Ice Scythe** :a: The ice scythe spins in place, covering a 10-foot emanation, and dealing 2d8 slashing plus 2d8 cold damage.  Creatures in the area must make a DC 27 Reflex saving throw.
**Critical Success** The creature takes no damage.
**Success** The creature takes half damage.
**Failure** The creature takes full damage.
**Critical Failure** The creature takes double damage and has -10 foot status penalty to its Speeds for 1 minute.
)

##### Hazards Added Since 23.12

##### Monsters Modified Since 23.12
* **Armos Knight**
  - Modified **Unleash Spikes** ability to have the armos Stride then Strike.
* **Armos Warrior**
  - Made the armos warriors not mindless as in game it is capable of talking to Link
* **Baby Dodongo**, **Kodongo**, **Young Dodongo**, and **King Dodongo**
  - All dodongos should now have at least some Athletics skill, with the Baby Dodongo being granted Acrobatics as well
* **Blizzagia**
  - Added Athletics skill which was missing
* **Boss Bokoblin**
  - Added **War Horn** ability to let the boss bokoblin act as a leader of bokoblins in combat
* **Heedle**
  - Added skills which were missing.  Specified slam does bludgeoning damage, forgot to add that.
* **Hinox**
  - Made the Hinox huge and gave its fist Strike a reach of 10 feet, mostly to fit the Stalnox being Huge
* **Horriblin**
  - Reduced base horriblin to level 2 from 4, removed rock attack as only blue horriblins and up threw large rocks
* **Grim Repoe**
  - Made the grim repoe Large instead of Small, correcting an oversight
* **Lizalfos, Aeralfos, Dinolfos, Fiery Aeralfos, Super Aeralfos**
  - Gave all lizal the Hylian language since in Hyrule Warriors they are capable of speaking in Hylian
* **Snapper, War Snapper, Stalchild, Stalhound, and Stalkoblin**
  - Added skills to the listed statblocks that were missing them.
=
##### Monsters Modified Since 23.12 Continued
* **Stone Talus**
  - Modified to hit bonuses of the strikes on the Stone Talus to be +14 so it isn't lower than the lower level smaller frost pebblit.
  - Modified AC to be 21 instead of 20 so it's more than the frost pebblit
  - Renamed slam to fist and gave fist strike a range of 10 feet befitting its large size
* **Volatile Chuchu**
  - Gave the volatile chuchu an Athletics skill
* **Wallmaster**
  - Added Stealth as a skill.
* **Wosu**
  - Added Hopping Stride action to the wosu
=
#### 23.12
##### General Changes
* Made changes to fit the Remastered rules with exception of alignment removal
  - Renamed flat-footed to off-guard
  - Replaced evil damage with spirit damage with the unholy trait
  - Replaced *positive* with *vitalic* and *negative* with *void*
  - Replaced **Attack of Opportunity** with **Reactive Strike**
  - Removed all instances of spell schools (conjuration, evocation, transmutation, etc.)
  - Leaving alignment in for all statblocks for legacy reasons, if wanting to play with full Remaster rules, just ignore the alignment of creatures

##### Monsters Modified since 23.10
* **Ache**
 - Reduced fangs damage from 1d10+4 to 1d8+4
 - Modified to mostly fit the Remaster changes, replacing evil damage with spirit damage with the unholy trait, giving them the unholy trait, though keeping alignment for legacy reasons
* **Acheman**
 - Increased claws to hit bonus from +13 to +15
 - Modified to mostly fit the Remaster changes, replacing evil damage with spirit damage with the unholy trait, giving them the unholy trait, though keeping alignment for legacy reasons
* **Deku Baba**
 - Changed to a hazard from a creature.  Upped to hit on jaws from +6 to +8 and upped Hit Points from 13 to 20.
* **Taros**
  - Modified to mostly fit the Remaster changes, giving them the unholy trait, though keeping alignment for legacy reasons
* **Sooga, Right Hand of the Inverted Eye and Yiga Footsoldier**
  - Removed verbal "trait" and cooldown on the **Yiga Assault** ability.
* **Wolfos and White Wolfos**
  - Changed Reckless Assault to make strikes at a -2 penalty based on playtesting.

##### Monsters Modified since 23.09
* **Aquamentus**
   - Changed physical resistance 7 to non-magical physical resistance 7 and gave the aquamentus magical physical resistance 4 so that magic weapons can bypass some, but not all, of the aquamentus's resistances
   - Added range of 50 feet to the aquamentus's fire bolt ranged Strike
   - Specified that **Tridirectional Beam** makes three fire bolt Strikes at three different targets so it cannot use all three on a single target with no MAP
* **Argorok**
   - Added Shadow trait to Argorok to represent it being corrupted by the Twili magic of the Fused Shadow
* **Big Eeno**
   - Fixed Reflex save and Will save to be +11 up from the copy-paste error of +6
* **Eyegore**
   - Removed eyegore's previous resistances and replaced with **Construct Armor** and Hardness of 10
          - Breaking the Construct Armor reduces eyegore's AC from 27 to 23
   - Reduced eyegore's to hit with eye beam to moderate (+18) from high (+20)
  - Reduced eyegore's HP from 140 to 120 to compensate for Hardness being higher than previous resistances
* **Fiery Aeralfos**
   - Added Fire trait to Fiery Aeralfos
* **Fire Gimos**
   - Renamed from Gimos to Fire Gimos
* **Ice Gimos**
   - Renamed from Gimos to Ice Gimos
* **Gohma**
   - Reduced weakness of weak point strikes from weakness 10 to weakness 5 to better match its level
=
